Current Commentary

Hua on the Resumption of Diplomatic Relations Between Hungary and the Soviet Union

According to foreign news, the treaty on the resumption of diplomatic relations between Hungary and the Soviet Union was formally signed on February 6 at the Soviet Embassy in Rome. From then on, the normal diplomatic relations between Hungary and the Soviet Union could be restored, and the countries of the Little Entente in Central Europe seemed likely to follow Hungary's example and continue to conclude treaties with the Soviet Union in the near future, establishing normal diplomatic relations. If we compare this with the recent diplomatic changes in Central Europe, such as the conclusion of the German-Polish Non-Aggression Pact, the conflicts between Germany and Austria, and the ongoing Austrian-Hungarian talks, we can see that the rapprochement between Hungary and the Soviet Union is not only the establishment of the Soviet Union's plan to encircle Germany, but also the beginning of the increasingly acute dual relationship between German-French conflict and German-Italian rivalry. The Soviet Union is looking far ahead, maneuvering among the countries, aiming to control Hitler, the anti-Soviet vanguard, through the countries of Central Europe and prevent him from crossing the Danube. Its diplomatic tactics can be described as agile, and the future direction of European diplomatic relations and the changes in world peace are closely related to this. Can the world ignore it?

Hungary is a new country formed after the disintegration of the Austro-Hungarian Empire. Its land area is less than 40,000 square miles, and its population does not exceed nine million, but it is located in the center of the Danube River basin, fertile and suitable for agriculture, and its industry is developed. In terms of market relations, it and Austria, Czechoslovakia, Romania, and other countries are the targets of competition for European powers, and especially Germany. Since the establishment of the Treaty of Versailles, the resources of the Danube River have been meat on the chopping block for others. This is a great and fatal wound to the development of German capitalism. For ten years after the war, it was bound by others and could not succeed. After Hitler took office, he tried his best to use his party members in the countries of Central Europe, hoping to establish a majority of allied countries to create a kindred regime. In fact, he wanted to encompass Central Europe and restore the old country, and then rely on this to ask the whole of Europe. His plan can be described as great. In January of this year, Hitler signed a ten-year non-aggression pact with Poland. Given the long-standing disputes between Germany and Poland, Hitler was able to endure it as much as possible. We knew early on that he had other plans. Negatively, it was to stabilize the eastern neighbors; positively, it was to invade Central Europe to the south. Sure enough, before long, there were signs of National Socialist Party members in Austria attempting to seize power, which eventually led Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss to appeal to the League of Nations. Hitler's ambitious plans are indeed astonishing, but the means by which others respond to them, such as the Soviet Union, are even more ingenious than Hitler's.

Hitler's active invasion of Central Europe is deeply hated by France on the one hand, and especially worried by Italy on the other. Therefore, France controls the countries of Central Europe and the Balkans with the Little Entente and the Four-Power Pact, while Italy befriends Austria, Hungary, Czechoslovakia, and other countries to control Hitler's expansion of power in the Danube River basin. The Soviet Union takes advantage of this to form a strong front encircling Germany. After the resumption of diplomatic relations between Hungary and the Soviet Union, the development of this situation is even more clear. Since Litvinov returned to the United States via Rome, people in the know knew early on that he had some plans for anti-German plans. After the conclusion of the German-Polish Non-Aggression Pact, it was even more known that diplomatic relations in Central Europe would become more tense. Will Hitler, under this situation of being forced into this situation, use all his strength to plan for further progress in Central Europe, or will he build strong allies outside of Europe to break through this encirclement? This is a question that deserves attention.

Balkan Pact Signed Amidst Joyful Church Bells

Mutual Guarantee of Border Security

Treaty Valid for Five Years

Bulgaria's Failure to Join is a Shortcoming

Athens The new Balkan Pact signed by the four countries of Greece, Romania, Turkey and Yugoslavia, was officially signed here today, as the church bells rang out and the military bands of the four countries played their national anthems to the cheers of the people. The pact is limited to five years, stipulates mutual guarantee of borders, and calls for unified action on all matters involving the interests of the signatory countries. Bulgaria did not sign, but the special concessions obtained by Yugoslavia in the pact should alleviate Greece's attitude. Three days ago, Greek semi-official circles stated that the Greek government's attitude towards the pact was that Greece would rather sign a mutual non-aggression agreement established within the framework of the League of Nations and in accordance with the Kellogg-Briand Pact. This is the most appropriate way to consolidate Balkan peace. It is also heard that the treaty stipulates that the countries should economically and politically oppose any revision of the Treaty of Versailles. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

French Parties United to Form Coalition Cabinet for the Nation

Premier Doumergue; Foreign Affairs: Barthou

Petain and Pietri in Charge of the Army and Navy

Gathering the National Intellectual Elite

Former Cabinet Ministers Occupy Five Seats

(Paris) The cabinet lineup began in the afternoon and is generally as follows: Premier Doumergue, Minister of Justice Cheron (former Minister of Finance), Minister of Interior Sarraut (former Premier), Minister of Finance Germain-Martin (former Budget Minister), Minister of Foreign Affairs Barthou (former Premier), Minister of the Army General Petain, Minister of the Navy Pietri (former Minister of Finance), Minister of Aviation General Denain, Minister of Labor Marant (leader of the right wing), Minister of Public Works Flandin (former Minister of Finance), Minister of Colonies Laval (former Premier), Minister of Agriculture Theydiou (former Premier), Minister of Commerce Herriot (former Premier), Minister of National Education Dervaux (former Minister of Pensions). (Havas Dispatch, 9th)

(Paris) Since the Socialist Party is unwilling to support, Doumergue fears that he will not be able to form a government of national unity. General Petain declared that although he dislikes hearing politics, if he is appointed as Minister of the Army, he will handle military affairs pragmatically. After meeting with Doumergue today, various political leaders expressed optimism. The new cabinet is expected to be formed this afternoon. The Communist Party plans to hold a large rally on Republic Road tonight to condemn Fascism, which has been banned by the Paris Police Chief. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

Act in Accordance with the Constitution

(Paris) Doumergue left his quiet homeland and re-entered politics to work for the country. When he arrived in the capital, the public regarded him as a savior and paid him respectful salutes. Because Mr. Doumergue is already seventy years old, taking on the country's difficult tasks at an old age has made people even more admire his spirit of righteousness. Mr. Doumergue declared in his old friend Briand's office at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: (I am not a revolutionary; I will act in accordance with the Constitution. As for whether the Constitution should be amended, that is another matter).

The Premier Does Not Concurrently Hold a Ministerial Post

After arriving in the capital, Doumergue did not rest and immediately began forming a cabinet, promising to complete it within twelve hours. Mr. Doumergue warned visitors that he was not a magician and did not believe in magic. His assumption of the premiership does not include holding a ministerial post concurrently so that he can freely deal with everything. Mr. Doumergue followed the usual practice of first seeking the opinions of the speakers of both the Senate and the House of Representatives.

Each Party is Willing to Provide Support

Internationally renowned French politicians have agreed to support Doumergue. The Radical Party in the House of Representatives has also asked Herriot to declare to Doumergue that he is willing to provide assistance. However, the attitude of the Radical Party cannot be relied upon until it is decided after the meeting.

Cautiously Selecting the Minister of Finance

Last night, according to reliable sources, Doumergue has abandoned the idea of recruiting former prime ministers to organize a new cabinet and does not want to form a government (outside of parliament). Mr. Doumergue, seeing that the instability of the budget has been one of the main reasons for the failure of previous cabinets, has invited the famous former Minister of Finance Caillaux, who has served as premier and finance minister, to consult. Mr. Caillaux is also a seventy-year-old man.

Like a General Returning in Triumph

After Doumergue was ordered to form a cabinet, all parties believed that the possibility of revolution had been averted. Mr. Doumergue met with President Lebrun for fifteen minutes yesterday and briefly described his plan, and then began work. At the same time, a large number of workers were cleaning up various commemorative objects abandoned by rioters in the streets in the past two days. On the way to the Presidential Palace and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Mr. Doumergue's scene was like a general returning in triumph, and those who saw him cheered and saluted. In the afternoon, Mr. Doumergue had a long talk with Daladier, who is nominally still the prime minister before the new cabinet is formed.

Before Doumergue arrived in the capital, Daladier urged President Lebrun to declare martial law, but was rejected.

The People's Hearts are Greatly Comforted

After Mr. Doumergue took on the difficult task of forming a cabinet, the people's hearts were greatly comforted. This afternoon and evening, crowds stood in front of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for several hours, eager to know the names of the new cabinet members selected by Mr. Doumergue. Troops were stationed in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs square to prevent a recurrence of the riot, but the crowds were orderly, quite different from two days ago.

The Imperial System Has Long Been Abandoned

At the same time, Xavier, who resides in Belgium and calls himself the King of the French Empire, issued a declaration, respectfully informing the French parties, classes, and races, saying, (The time has come to re-implement the imperial system on which France's greatness is based). Parisians dismissed this declaration with indifference. Qualified observers expressed their opinions, saying that imperialism, like communism, has been abandoned by French politics. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

The Political Situation Has Taken on a New Atmosphere

The Disturbances in Paris Have Suddenly Subsided

The General Strike is Scheduled for Monday

Aims to Uphold Democracy and Oppose Dictatorship

(Paris) The prelude to Doumergue's formation of a cabinet has given France a new atmosphere. Not only have disturbances subsided everywhere, but also French bonds and other securities have changed their old appearance in the market today and prices have risen. The new Prime Minister has received the full support of the Senate, and the House of Representatives, with the exception of the Socialist Party, the Communist Party, and a small number of Radicals, also supports Mr. Doumergue. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

(Paris) This afternoon, when factories and shops closed, the situation was peaceful. Many curious people patrolled the places where disturbances occurred in the past two days, pointing and describing the incidents in detail, without excitement. The general public generally expressed sympathy for the move to appoint former President Doumergue to form a cabinet. In the evening, the capital was peaceful as usual. Only in outlying provinces such as Lyon were there still demonstrations, but no serious incidents occurred. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) The National Confederation of Labor issued a notice, advising all workers to stop working for twenty-four hours on Monday, which is intended to show that if anyone attempts to replace democracy with a dictatorship, the people will never sit idly by. General Secretary Stonhouse of the National Confederation of Labor declared that the purpose of the general strike movement by the National Confederation of Labor is not to disrupt the country and to allow the public to peacefully express its will only. The Postal Workers' Union, the Civil Servants' Union, the National Union of Elementary School Teachers, and the Education Union have all issued orders to hold a general strike for twenty-four hours on Monday. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

Allied Support for Austrian Independence Resonates

Rome Prepares Similar Declaration

German-Austrian Dispute Submitted to League of Nations

Considered Inopportune at Present

Documents on Austrian Case Sent to Major Powers to Clarify the Truth

Rome - It was recently announced in the British House of Commons that maintaining Austria's independence is the foundation of British foreign policy. This declaration is warmly welcomed here, and it is not impossible that a similar declaration may be made. People here believe that the only good policy regarding the current situation in Austria is to assist Austria in defending its independence, provide Austria with economic convenience, and enable Austria to have more contact with other Central European countries. As for Austria's political system, it is believed that National Socialism is a mysterious force, and Austria must resist it with another mysterious force. Furthermore, there is approval of the Austrian Chancellor's visit to Budapest, but it is not considered to be of great significance. In addition, Italy still considers it inappropriate for Austria to submit the German-Austrian dispute to the League of Nations, but if Austria insists on submitting it to the League of Nations, Italy will likely act in concert with other countries that support Austrian independence. (Havas News Agency, 9th)

(London) - The Austrian State Council recently decided to allow Chancellor Dollfuss to submit the dispute between Germany and Austria to the League of Nations, and sent a thick file of documents on this matter to the major powers to clarify the truth. Today, the Austrian Minister to Britain delivered these documents to the Foreign Office. (Havas News Agency, 8th)

Austrian Chancellor's Visit to Budapest a Success

Return Trip Temporarily Postponed

Rome - Today's local newspapers reported that Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss and Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös discussed various issues concerning the interests of both countries, with completely satisfactory results. It is said that both prime ministers agreed to continue the current policies that have yielded satisfactory results, believing that the current administrative and economic cooperation between the two countries is not only beneficial to both countries, but also benefits the peace of all of Europe. The Hungarian Regent presented the Austrian Chancellor with the highest Cross of Merit. (National Telegram, 8th)

Budapest - Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss, who came here a few days ago to hold talks with Prime Minister Gömbös, was originally scheduled to return home last night, but temporarily postponed his trip to today due to feeling slightly unwell. However, some sources claim that Dollfuss' postponement of his return was actually due to worrying news coming from Vienna. Whether this is true remains to be seen. (Havas Telegram, 9th)

Vienna - On September 10th of last year, Chancellor Dollfuss delivered an important political speech, saying that he would reject Marxism and National Socialism, maintain Austria's freedom and independence, and reform the constitution based on a professional group system. Recently, the Patriotic League of Tyrol Province launched a movement demanding that Dollfuss fully implement the reform measures he announced. This movement spread rapidly, and today the Patriotic Leagues of the provinces of Carinthia and Salzburg have joined. The leaders of the League will directly present their demands to Chancellor Dollfuss. (Havas Telegram, 8th)

Political Crisis in Austria

Home Guard Controls Administration of Two Provinces

Leftists Will Fight to Protect Themselves

Vienna - In view of the fact that the Home Guard has obtained full jurisdiction after implementing political changes in Tyrol and Upper Austria, implementing a semi-military administrative system, it is now implementing the same actions in the provinces of Styria and Burgenland, demanding the provincial governors: (1) to form a provincial government that is independent of political parties and should include representatives of the Home Guard; (2) to remove disloyal officials; (3) to appoint political affairs officers to unstable cities; (4) to appoint idle officials of the Home Guard as county magistrates; (5) to disband groups that resist the state. The provincial governors are currently dealing with them in a moderate manner, saying that they do not have the power to comply with the demands and must seek instructions from Vienna. It is expected that the leader of the Vienna Home Guard, Vice-Chancellor Fey, will lead a delegation to appear in the city council tomorrow to make the same demands. The Socialist Party and the Communist Party will fight to protect themselves today. It is said that if the Home Guard uses force, Vienna will be engulfed in flames. (National Telegram, 8th)

US Ambassador Bullitt to Take Office in Russia at the End of the Month

Progress in Trade Negotiations Between the Two Countries

(Washington) - After the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia, the first US Ambassador to Russia, Bullitt, went to Russia at the end of last year to present his credentials and make some arrangements, then returned to the United States to report to President Roosevelt on the process. Recently, Bullitt was scheduled to board a ship on February 15th to cross the ocean and take office in Russia. In addition, there has been significant progress in the negotiations between the United States and Russia on the debts owed to the United States by the Tsarist Russia, as well as other disputed points, and the trade agreement between the two countries. (Havas Telegram, 8th)

Russo-Italian Friendship

Extension of Trade Agreement Approved Through Exchange of Documents

Rome - The commercial agreement signed between Italy and Russia on May 6, 1933, was extended on December 5th of last year by representatives of the two countries signing a document. Today, Prime Minister Mussolini and the Soviet Russian Ambassador to Italy, Potemkin, exchanged ratification documents. Today is the tenth anniversary of the restoration of diplomatic relations between Italy and Russia. The Soviet Russian Ambassador said to the Italian Prime Minister that the Soviet Russian government was satisfied with the extension of the commercial agreement, which will further consolidate the friendship between the two nations. Potemkin also said (the friendship between Italy and Russia can be regarded as a major factor in maintaining peace). In addition, Soviet Russia will soon restore diplomatic relations with Hungary (recently, the Hungarian Minister to Turkey, Junger, exchanged documents with the Soviet Russian Ambassador Potemkin in Rome, recognizing Soviet Russia), and is deeply grateful for Italy's assistance. The Soviet Russian Ambassador expressed his gratitude to the Italian Prime Minister. Mussolini replied that Italy is willing to pursue a friendly policy with Russia in both political and economic terms. Since the restoration of diplomatic relations between the two countries ten years ago, Italy has always held this policy, and hopes that this policy can be further developed within the next ten years. (Havas Telegram, 8th)

No Understanding Reached Between Britain and France, Trade War Inevitable

Britain Will Impose Retaliatory Taxes on France

(London) - If France does not abolish its current severe attitude towards British imports before Monday, British customs will take retaliatory measures against France on that day. According to reliable sources today, if Britain and France cannot reach an understanding before the 12th, Britain will impose retaliatory tariffs on all French goods imported into the British Empire from that day onwards. If a trade war is inevitable, Britain has already implemented an economic war against the two countries, one being Ireland, both of which use tariffs as barriers to prevent the entry of goods. As of now, France has not shown any signs of retreating from Britain's demands. If a trade war is implemented, both sides will inevitably suffer losses, as France purchases millions of pounds worth of British goods each year. (Reuters, 9th)

German Economy Stable

Budget Surplus

Effect of Austerity Measures

(Berlin) - At a time when governments of various countries are facing financial difficulties, the German government alone has had a surplus since the beginning of the new year. This is not only a good phenomenon that has not been seen in Germany for many years, but also a unique economic stability situation in the world. Germany implemented austerity policies from the beginning of last year, and tax revenues were also quite strong, so the national treasury still had a surplus of 16.3 million marks at the end of the year. This shows that various industries in Germany have entered a period of recovery, and it is also clear evidence that the government's war on unemployment is gradually becoming effective. (National Telegram, 8th)

Gold Flows Steadily to the United States

(New York) - Since the implementation of the President's gold purchase plan, large quantities of gold have been imported into the United States every day. Today, the German postal ship Bremen arrived in New York, bringing gold bars worth 13 million yuan from various ports in Europe. The Panamanian liner will arrive tomorrow, carrying a large number of gold bars. According to the reasons for this round of gold inflow, one is due to the President's new monetary policy to collect gold, and the other is due to the gradual peace of the French political situation and the unrest in the political situation of various European countries. (National Telegram, 8th)

Japanese House of Peers Rejects Fascism

Prime Minister's Answer is Abstract

(Tokyo) - The House of Peers plenary session continued to meet at 1:45 PM today. First, Viscount Maeda Toshisada raised a question:

Regarding the issue of thought, that is, the issue of Fascism, raised by Mr. Seki Naohiko a few days ago, the government's answer at the time was quite unsatisfactory. Please explain in detail.

Prime Minister's answer:

The government is indeed trying to guide it well, in order to incorporate it into the correct track of constitutional government.

Mr. Maeda then raised the following three points:

(1) The Prime Minister seems to have the intention of guiding Fascist thought well. Then, what is its countermeasure?

(2) Has the government added a countermeasure for Fascism in the consultation plan of the Thought Countermeasures Committee?

(3) If it has been added, please explain its content.

Prime Minister's answer:

Regarding guiding thought, it is not limited to Fascism. It is entirely based on the fundamental spirit of impartiality and justice, and various efforts are made. Therefore, the Thought Countermeasures Consultative Council is also based on the above purpose.

Viscount Maeda stood up from his seat and said:

The Prime Minister's answer is entirely abstract and is too simple.

The Prime Minister did not answer further. The general question war on the speeches of the Ministers of State ended here. The meeting adjourned at 2:34 PM. (Japan United Press, 9th)

(Tokyo) - Today, Mr. Kono Ichiro of the Seiyukai Party spoke in the fourth subcommittee of the House of Representatives as follows:

The military has published an opinion on the rural problem in the name of the Minister. Is it within the scope of application? Please explain.

Minister of the Army Hayashi answered:

The army's opinion on the rural problem outside its jurisdiction should be considered a mistake. I intend to absolutely not do this again from now on.

The Minister of the Army's statement of this attitude has attracted the attention of the general public. (Japan United Press, 9th)

(Tokyo) - Minister of the Navy Osumi stated the following in response to a question raised by Mr. Yakaku Saburo of the Seiyukai Party regarding the issue of arms reduction in the fourth subcommittee of the House of Representatives' budget today:

(1) Ensure the security of Japan's national defense.

(2) Advocate amending the existing arms reduction treaty.

(3) Japan's national defense is not for invading others, but for defending itself.

(4) Maintaining the superiority of only one country, such arms reduction is unfair, so it is necessary to advocate the formulation of a fair and appropriate concrete plan. (Japan United Press, 9th)

French Train Derailment Again

More Than Forty Dead and Injured

(Paris) - Today, a train accident occurred again in France. A train carrying miners collided with a light locomotive. Almost the entire rear of the train was destroyed. Fortunately, the number of deaths was not high. Only three people died and forty were injured, many of whom were seriously injured. After the accident, ambulances rushed to the scene and sent the injured to the hospital for treatment. (Reuters, 8th)

Merger of Two British Shipping Companies

Government Loans for New Ships

Develop North Atlantic Routes

(London) - Financial Under-Secretary Bailey Shaw reported in the House of Commons this afternoon that the British Cunard Steamship Company and the Oceanic Steam Navigation Company have reached an agreement to merge the North Atlantic Cunard and White Star routes. The Ministry of Finance has allowed a loan of 9.5 million pounds to the new shipping group based on this agreement. One part of the loan is to complete a large passenger ship that the Cunard Company has been building for two years, and the remainder will likely be used to build similar passenger ships. The British government has allowed this agreement to take effect, but on the main condition that the new shipping group is still managed by British people. (Havas Telegram, 8th)

Guangdong Provincial and Municipal Banknotes Plummet

(Hong Kong) With the Lunar New Year approaching, the financial situation in Guangdong City is turbulent again. The provincial and municipal banknotes have plummeted. The Commercial and Business Coordination Council has sent a letter to the Silver Industry Association to open the market ahead of schedule for the Lunar New Year. (Central News Agency, 9th)

Naval Expert Ackworth Elaborates on the British Navy and the Future War

If War Breaks Out in 1936

Japan Will Inevitably Occupy Hong Kong, Singapore, and Australia

Britain Can Be Fearless if it Rushes to Build Cruisers

(London) - Naval Captain Ackworth has written a book on naval issues, titled (The British Navy and the Future War). Ackworth is a naval expert, and his book criticizes the weaknesses of the British Navy, saying that Britain has historically shouldered a major mission in the world, especially in the Far East, but its navy is far inferior to Japan's. The author specifically criticizes the (Rodney)-class armored ships and the newly built (Dan Steel) destroyer, saying that the armament and speed of these warships are insufficient and cannot cope with war. Ackworth concludes that if the British Navy does not change its course, the consequences of a British-Japanese war in 1936 will be disastrous. Once a war breaks out in the Far East, Japan will attack Hong Kong. The main force of the British Navy is 10,000 nautical miles away, and Hong Kong is a base that is completely unsuitable for defense. Once contact is made, there is no chance of winning. Because the Japanese Navy is currently preparing for war, its attack on Hong Kong will carry marines. On the fourth day after the war, Hong Kong will be surrounded, and within fifteen days, Hong Kong will no longer belong to the British. Once Hong Kong is lost, Singapore will inevitably fall into the hands of the Japanese, and even Australia will become a part of Japan's possession. Ackworth concludes that the most suitable warship for modern naval needs is an armored cruiser of more than 11,000 tons, with a speed of 17.5 nautical miles per hour, equipped with 13.5-inch caliber guns. Ackworth believes that if the British Far East Fleet, excluding second-class warships, has 15 more armored cruisers of the above type, it can be fearless. When war breaks out, the British Far East Fleet can rely on its own strength to threaten the communication of the Japanese fleet before the reinforcements sent by the home country arrive, and prevent it from succeeding. Ackworth also strongly advocates that the British fleet should use coal as fuel in the future (as opposed to using heavy oil). (Havas Telegram, 8th)

(London) - Today, the British Admiralty officially denied the news published in the Rainer's Illustrated News last Sunday, saying that the Royal Navy conference held in Singapore this time had resolved to build a solid naval base between the Falkland Islands, so that when a conflict occurs between Japan and the United States in the future, Britain can protect its rights in the Far East. The report also claimed that if Japan and the United States go to war, the Panama Canal will be blocked, so Britain will contact the Australian and New Zealand fleets, build fortifications between the Falkland Islands, and protect British ships that can pass through the Strait of Magellan. (National Telegram, 9th)

Russian Army Ready for Battle

Declaration by the Commander of the Red Army in the Far East

Reval - According to Moscow reports, General Blyukher, Commander of the Russian Army in the Far East, made a boastful speech during a large-scale review held today to commemorate the 17th Communist Party Congress. After Blyukher declared his loyalty to Stalin and endorsed the policies of the Communist Party, he went on to say that the entire Russian army is ready for battle and ready to cope with emergencies. If Russia is attacked, our army can fulfill its responsibility without any effort. At the same time, the War Revolutionary Committee issued an order to the army to praise Stalin and said that the Red Army is the only army in the world that does not practice imperialism or occupy foreign land. The Red Army is combined with the National Party, and its sole purpose is to safeguard peace. However, our blades have been sharpened, and we will slay anyone who attempts to endanger the peaceful efforts of our socialist land. We will annihilate anyone who attempts to cross the border. (National Telegram, 9th)

Former US Aviation Director Strongly Advocates Expanding the Air Force

US Private Aircraft Factories Make Huge Profits

(Washington) - The House of Representatives Aviation Committee recently received a report stating that aircraft manufacturers made a profit of 90 percent on orders from the army in 1932. In addition, from 1928 to the first few months of 1933, the factory sold aircraft worth a total of US$45,529,000 to the army. The House Aviation Committee is currently investigating this matter. Colonel Mitchell, the former aviation director who resigned in 1926, fiercely attacked the government's policy of entrusting private companies to manufacture military aircraft in the House Aviation Committee, saying that the US Air Force is equivalent to nothing compared to Europe. This is the truth, but the general public is afraid to say it. Mitchell also criticized former Presidents Coolidge and Hoover for failing to develop military aviation. He then attacked the naval battleship construction policy, saying that only aircraft and submarines would be useful in future wars. Finally, Mitchell advocated that air stations must be built in Alaska, Hawaii, and the Philippines. (Havas Telegram, 9th)

(Nanjing) - The Constitutional Drafting Committee held its 20th meeting at 2:00 PM on the 9th, chaired by Sun Ke. The central political system was discussed, but not completed. The next meeting will continue the discussion. (Central News Agency, 9th)

Provisional Organizational Regulations for the Palace Museum

Passed by the Legislative Yuan

(Nanjing) - The Provisional Organizational Regulations for the National Peiping Palace Museum, passed by the Legislative Yuan at its 46th meeting on the morning of the 9th, are as follows:

Article 1: The National Peiping Palace Museum is directly under the Executive Yuan of the National Government and is responsible for the preservation, opening, and dissemination of buildings, antiques, books, and archives in the Forbidden City and its affiliated Dagao Hall, Qing Taimiao, Jingshan Huangshicheng, and Shiludaiku.

Article 2: The National Peiping Palace Museum shall establish the following offices: (1) General Affairs Office, (2) Antiquities Museum, (3) Library, (4) Archives Museum.

Article 3: The responsibilities of the General Affairs Office are as follows: (1) Matters relating to all confidential matters, (2) Matters relating to the custody of seals, (3) Matters relating to drafting, receiving, and sending documents and meeting minutes, (4) Matters relating to accounting, general affairs, and engineering repairs, (5) Matters relating to the inspection and security of the museum, (6) Matters relating to publication, (7) Other matters not belonging to other museums.

Article 4: The responsibilities of the Antiquities Museum are as follows: (1) Matters relating to the preservation and display of antiques, (2) Matters relating to the identification and cataloging of antiques, (3) Matters relating to the dissemination and photography of antiques, (4) Matters relating to the exhibition of antiques, (5) Matters relating to the publication of antiques.

Article 5: The responsibilities of the Library are as follows: (1) Matters relating to the preservation and display of books, (2) Matters relating to the classification and cataloging of books, (3) Matters relating to the reading of books, (4) Matters relating to the textual research of book versions, (5) Matters relating to the reproduction and dissemination of rare books.

Article 6: The responsibilities of the Archives Museum are as follows: (1) Matters relating to the sorting and cataloging of Ming and Qing archives, historical records, and historical items, (2) Matters relating to the preservation and display of Ming and Qing archives, historical records, and historical items, (3) Matters relating to the collection, sorting, and editing of Ming and Qing historical materials, (4) Matters relating to the classification, photography, and editing of historical items.

Article 7: The National Peiping Palace Museum shall have one Director, appointed by the government, who, upon the order of the Executive Yuan, and in accordance with the resolutions of the Board of Directors, shall be responsible for the overall management of the Museum and its affiliated offices.

Article 8: The National Peiping Palace Museum shall have one Director of the Office, recommended for appointment, and three Directors of the Museums, who shall be appointed by the Director after being decided upon by the Board of Directors. They shall be responsible for the management of the General Affairs Office and the Museums under the order of the Director of the Museum. There shall be eight to eleven Section Chiefs, recommended for appointment, and twenty-eight to thirty-six staff members, appointed.

Article 9: The National Peiping Palace Museum may, when necessary, have one or two secretaries recommended for appointment, twenty-six to thirty-six staff members to handle affairs, and may employ employees as appropriate.

Article 10: The National Peiping Palace Museum may establish various specialized committees when necessary for academic purposes.

Article 11: The National Peiping Palace Museum shall have a Board of Directors, which, in addition to the Minister of the Interior and the Minister of Education as ex officio directors, shall consist of seventeen to twenty-seven directors, who shall be unpaid and appointed by the Executive Yuan.

Article 12: The Board of Directors shall have one Chairman and four to six Managing Directors, all of whom shall be elected by the Board of Directors and reported to the Executive Yuan for record. The Board of Directors shall have one Secretary, who shall be elected from among the directors by the Board of Directors and shall be responsible for the internal documents and matters assigned by the Board of Directors.

Article 13: The National Peiping Palace Museum shall have the following matters decided by the Board of Directors: (1) Matters relating to the preservation and disposal of items, (2) Matters relating to the budget, final accounts, and custody of funds, (3) Matters relating to the establishment of specialized committees, (4) Other important matters. The resolutions of the preceding paragraph shall be reported to the Executive Yuan and announced.

Article 14: The rules of procedure of the Board of Directors shall be determined by the Board of Directors and reported to the Executive Yuan for record.

Article 15: The detailed rules for the operation of the National Peiping Palace Museum shall be drafted by the Director of the Museum, submitted to the Board of Directors for decision, and reported to the Executive Yuan for record.

Article 16: These Regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency, 9th)

Meeting of the Legislative Yuan

Investigating Taxes and Fees in Various Provinces and Cities

(Nanjing) - The Legislative Yuan held its 46th meeting of the 3rd session on the 9th, attended by Fang Juehui, Wang Qi, and other 70 people, chaired by Sun Ke, with Liang Hancao as Secretary-General. Matters discussed: (1) The 391st meeting of the Central Political Council resolved that the Public Officials Registration Regulations were approved in principle and sent to the Legislative Yuan by the National Government for handling. Resolved to be referred to the Legal System Committee for review. (2) The 392nd meeting of the Central Political Council resolved that the Financial Consolidation Public Bond Regulations of Hubei Province in the 23rd year of the Republic of China were approved in principle and sent to the Legislative Yuan by the National Government for deliberation. Resolved to be referred to the Finance Committee for review. (3) Report of the Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan on the review of the general budget of local revenue and expenditure of Beijing Municipality for the 22nd year. Resolved to be passed according to the review report. (4) Report of the Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan on the review of the amendment to Article 6 of the Hubei Province Post-War Public Bond Regulations and the principal and interest repayment schedule in the 21st year of the Republic of China. Resolved to be passed according to the review report. (5) Lin Bin, Jiao Yitang, Peng Yangguang, Shi Shangkuan, Ma Chaojun, Chen Zhaoying, Liu Jianxun, Hu Xuanming, Luo Yunhuo, and Gu Zhenggang reported on the review of the draft regulations of the Central National Medical Center. Resolved to be re-referred for review. (6) The Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan suggested that the Legislative Yuan should consult the Executive Yuan and order all provinces and cities to report the following six items of all current taxes and fees: name, method, tax rate, amount of tax revenue, date of levy, and reasons for collection, to the Ministry of Finance before the end of June of this year, and submit them to the Executive Yuan for transfer to the Legislative Yuan for review. Resolved to be passed according to the proposed opinion. (7) The Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan suggested that the Legislative Yuan should request the National Government to order all central agencies to submit all taxes and fees collected and contracts concluded without legislative procedures to the Legislative Yuan for review before the end of April of this year in order to emphasize the spirit of the rule of law and comply with the government's orders. Resolution: Passed according to the proposed opinion. (8) The Legal System Committee of the Legislative Yuan reported on the review of the draft amended Organizational Law of the National Peiping Palace Museum and the Board of Directors Regulations. Resolution: Passed with amendments. (Central News Agency, 9th)

(Changsha) The bandit troops of Kong and Xiao retreated from the Huangsha Huanjiuxiantang area. The two divisions of Zhu and Yuan, along with Peng, have been continuously suppressing them for days, killing over a thousand bandits. Now, troops from all directions have arrived, under the command of Zhu Yaohua. A general siege will commence on the 7th. Furthermore, tungsten mines in Jiangxi and Guangdong will be nationalized. Hu Shixin has been appointed as the special commissioner for tungsten sand in southern Jiangxi for construction purposes. (9th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Local celebrities and figures are organizing a Yellow River disaster relief association. Xiao Ke's pseudo-Eighth Army has reportedly fled from northwestern Jiangxi to provide support. After the pseudo-Sixth Army Corps merged with Kong's bandits in Yifeng, the Zhu and Tao divisions are pursuing them eastward along separate routes.

The two bandit groups are attempting to flee north from Fengxin through Tonggu back to the border of Hunan and Hubei. They are engaged in fierce battles with the Western Route Army in the Shangmei area north of Yifeng. They are being subjected to relentless aerial and land bombardment. The provincial government has ordered the counties in western Jiangxi to relentlessly pursue the Kong, Xiao, and Gao factions as they flee north toward Gao'an, Fengxin, Xiushui, and Yifeng. All counties must collaborate with the stationed troops to firmly defend their cities, ensuring that the bandits have no room to breathe or loot, and not cease until they are completely eliminated. Cai Tingkai's Departure from the 19th Route Army

Cai Was Besieged by Militia in Shizhong

Guangdong Army's Huang Division Stationed in Yongding and Longyan

Xiamen Communication: Cai Tingkai's whereabouts have been unknown since he led his troops west to Longyan on January 21. According to recent sources from Shizhong and Longyan, Cai left Quanzhou for Zhangzhou on the morning of the 21st, with approximately 200 guards and a battalion of the Special Service Regiment under Li Jinbo. Upon arriving in Zhangzhou, together with 600-700 students from the Zhishan Military Officer Training Class, a regiment of the Fourth Army under Zhang Yan led by Zhou Lixing, and a regiment of the Political Guard Division under Xu Minghong, totaling over 4,000 men, and 20-odd trucks loaded with firearms, ammunition, and artillery shells, they proceeded to Shizhong via Nanjing. Before abandoning Zhangzhou, Xu Minghong also transported a portion of the ammunition stored in Zhangzhou to Hexi, which was also transported to Shizhong along the way. Cai and his troops arrived in Shizhong on the 23rd. Xu Minghong immediately led a regiment of the Guard Division to Longyan, while Cai led 2,000 troops to station in Shizhong without retreating. Cai believed that Longyan was an isolated city that could not be defended, and Shizhong was a natural stronghold with hundreds of well-known pillboxes. The location was also a strategic area where Longyan and Zhangzhou met, serving to defend against the Central Army from Zhangzhou and safeguard Longyan. Furthermore, the troops of Li from Anxi Chang'an could be received after their retreat, enabling both offensive and defensive operations, and also accommodating the troops coming from Quanzhou. After Cai arrived in Shizhong, he stationed himself in the largest and most famous Yangyun pillbox, deploying Shizhong's defenses. However, the leader of the Shizhong militia, who had been detained by Cai Tingkai for years, escaped from prison in Shizhong when Zhangzhou was in crisis. Xie Yangqi, the former head of the Shizhong militia, was commissioned by Yang Fengnian, the commander of the Southern Fujian Militia, as the commander of the Fifth Detachment of the Southern Fujian Anti-Rebel Army. Xie immediately mobilized the Shizhong militia to form the Anti-Rebel Army, first burning four wooden bridges above Shizhong leading to Longyan. Zhang Shiyu, the commander of the Fourth Detachment, also burned the bridges between Zhangzhou and Shizhong. On the 25th, Xie joined forces with the militia under Guo Xingmin, totaling approximately 2,000 men, surrounding the pillbox occupied by Cai. The people of Shizhong were extremely fierce, with guns in every household, and they were very familiar with the terrain. As a result, Cai and his troops were heavily besieged until the 28th.

Upon hearing the news in Longyan, Xu Minghong immediately sent Fu Baicui with his 2,000-strong Western Fujian Volunteer Corps from Shanghang to reinforce them, coordinating internal and external efforts. Cai then led his troops to break out of the encirclement and arrived at Daxiaochi southwest of Longyan on the 29th. Cai's original intention in staying in Shizhong was to receive the troops from Quanzhou, hoping to reorganize and form an army. However, the troops in Quanzhou were reorganized due to Mao Weishou and Zhang Yan's defection, and he was also trapped in Shizhong, deeply realizing that the situation was hopeless. Thus, he left the army on the 29th. Regarding Cai's whereabouts after leaving the army, some said he went to Changting, while others said he went to Fengshi in Shanghang and entered Chaozhou and Shantou towards Hong Kong. Judging from his telegram, he was not willing to defect to the communists, so it is more likely that he went to Guangdong and then to Hong Kong. After Xu Minghong arrived in Longyan, he ordered Fu Baicui to reinforce Cai while leading his own Guard Division and Volunteer Corps of 1,000-2,000 men west to Changting. Changting is still a bandit area, so it is rumored that Xu went to join the communists. After Xu left, no one was in charge of Longyan. After Cai retreated to Daxiaochi, he did not enter the city and left the army to go elsewhere. After Fu Baicui retreated, he returned to his hometown of Jiaoyang in Shanghang. Zhou Lixing led 2,000 troops to station in Daxiaochi. Therefore, since February 1, only a small number of the former Western Fujian Post-Rehabilitation Office Volunteer Corps remained in the city of Longyan. Other than that, there was not a single soldier. When Cai left the army, the Guangdong army had already entered Shanghang and Wuping. Zhou Lixing sent someone to request incorporation into the Guangdong army under Huang Renhuan. Huang then sent two regiments to station in Kanshi and one regiment to station in Yongding. On the 4th, dozens of vanguards of the Guangdong army entered the county seat of Longyan. According to someone from Yongding on the 6th, the First and Third Regiments of Zeng Youren's Brigade of Huang Renhuan's Division of the Guangdong army entered the county seat of Longyan on the 5th, while the Second Regiment entered the county seat of Yongding on the 4th, stationed inside and outside the county seat. Personnel from the former Western Fujian Post-Rehabilitation Office all fled. The people of Yongding elected Lin Yunbo as the county magistrate of Yongding. Since the Guangdong army entered the city of Longyan, the military has temporarily maintained order. Personnel from the former Western Fujian Post-Rehabilitation Office have fled with Xu Minghong. The Chamber of Commerce is convening meetings with various sectors, but no one has come forward to take on political affairs. (February 7th)

Situation After the Inauguration of the New Provincial Committee of Fujian

Xu Fu Temporarily Maintains the Department of Finance

Chiang Ting-wen is Deploying Troops to Suppress Bandits

Fuzhou Communication: Provincial government members Chen Yi, Zheng Zhenwen, Chen Ticheng, Xu Fu, Li Shijia, and Lin Zhiyuan were sworn in on the 5th. Various departments also began work on the 6th. The heads of the secretariat are all newly appointed, and most of the other staff members are old employees who have been re-employed. However, due to financial difficulties, the expenses of various agencies have been reduced by a quarter compared to the original budget, so the number of personnel has also been reduced by a third. Salaries are generally calculated from February, so most civil servants lose two months of salary, with some losing one month. However, Sun Jiaze, the director of the Department of Finance, is currently in Guangdong and has not yet arrived in Fujian. The position is temporarily held by Xu Fu, who is only willing to maintain it for a month. If Sun does not come again, the central government will be asked to appoint a special commissioner. It was previously rumored that Du Qiyun would be the director of the Fujian Security Office. Du came to the province a few days ago and met with Chen Yi on the 3rd. The military commission's order to revoke the title of military special envoy has been received. There are two views on the Security Office: one is that there is already a security commander, and the Security Office will be temporarily delayed; the other is that the Security Office will be scaled down and attached to the provincial government, with Chen Yi concurrently serving as the director, and the newly appointed security commander, Xiao Qian, flew from Hangzhou to the province on the afternoon of the 6th to meet with Chiang Ting-wen and Chen Yi to discuss the problem of organizing the provincial security

teams. The headquarters will likely be organized within a few days.

Regarding the bandit situation in northern Fujian, it was most rampant in late January, with four counties, Shunchang, Jiangle, Yong'an, and Shaxian, falling in succession. In the past ten days, through the concerted efforts of various armies in encirclement and suppression, the bandit momentum has gradually subsided. The Red bandits entrenched in Shaxian have been attacked from both sides by the Lu Xingbang and Leng Xin Divisions, and their strength has been depleted. They have already retreated towards Jiangle. The Leng Division is approaching the county seat. However, the county seat of Shouning in eastern Fujian has been captured by local Red bandits, who looted extensively, burning over a thousand shops. Yesterday, Chiang Ting-wen ordered the Chen Qixuan Division to send troops to suppress them. Furthermore, local communists in the coastal areas of Lianjiang County, such as Mabi, Toujie, and Feiluan, have been encircled and suppressed by the Wei Duo Regiment of the Marine Corps. Headquarters Promotes Political Education and Production Cooperation

Circular Orders to the Three Provinces, Instructing Four Points

Implementation Scheduled to Begin This March

Hankou Dispatch: The Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, on the 8th, issued circular orders to the three provincial governments, instructing four points regarding political education and production cooperation. The order states: (Politics, education, and production are fundamental tasks for national salvation today and are the foundation for national rejuvenation. Examining the great powers, after periods of destruction, they all quickly rose up to catch up, embedding production in education as an effective measure. Using each other for mutual benefit, striving to become strong, and working diligently are crucial for success. When the Commander-in-Chief oversaw Wuhan in previous years, he deeply understood that without clarifying politics, there would be no way to eliminate the source of chaos, and without smelting education and production into one furnace, there would be no way to achieve social stability. In the previous year, an order was issued as secret number 647, planning the construction of education cooperation, and subsequently, an order was issued as secret number 539, promulgating the general outlines of the principles for the implementation of political education, educational production, and productive education, all on record. Now, it is observed that many commissioners and the provincial departments of construction and education are able to implement these principles faithfully according to laws and regulations, but there are also those who are still planning or whose management is lacking. Further instructions are hereby given as follows: (1) Each commissioner's stationed location, if a farm or agricultural and forestry experimental school has not yet been prepared and established, a written plan must be drafted within ten days of the receipt of this order, submitted separately to the responsible agency for approval, and then presented for review; no further delays are allowed. (2) Rural lecture classes are especially important. If they have not been established in each commissioner's stationed location, they should be prepared immediately. In addition, each responsible agency should investigate and consider the conditions in each county and establish them as appropriate. (3) To cultivate a spirit of enduring hardship and service, teachers and students should all be practically engaged in cultivation. Therefore, the number of workers at each farm should be limited to two, and the number of workers at agricultural schools should be limited to four. Established farms and agricultural schools should implement this principle starting from March of the 23rd year. (4) The general outline of the principles for implementing political education, educational production, and productive education, items two, three, and four, are crucial to production education and political reform. Each commissioner's work reports and inspection reports should be carefully assessed and reported to the ministry item by item and article by article. The provincial departments of construction and education should especially assess each school, each factory, and each farm at any time to determine whether they are diligently improving according to the general outline of the principles, and they should report the improvement status at any time. The above-mentioned key points, in addition to being distributed separately, are hereby urgently ordered to be followed and implemented by the provincial governments, and all subordinates should be instructed to comply with them. The date of receipt of this document should be reported for verification. This order is of utmost importance.) (February 8th)

The Sichuan-Kangding Inspection Group Inspects the Construction of Beibei

|Various New Enterprises Are Highly Developed|

Shanghai Reporter: The Sichuan-Kangding Inspection Group arrived in Chongqing on the Democracy steamship on the afternoon of January 29th. On the 30th, they inspected the city and learned that Chongqing is built on a hillside, surrounded by water on three sides, making development difficult. However, the newly built roads outside the city are very impressive. The water company, which cost three million, is also very grand. The power plant, which is currently under construction, has a capacity of three thousand kilowatts, using steam turbine engines, and is very innovative. It is said that there is a waterfall two hundred li away in Changshou. If it could be used to generate electricity, it would have about three thousand horsepower available. There are also well-equipped schools and agricultural experimental fields, so the future is promising. On the afternoon of January 31st, various circles in Chongqing held a welcoming party at the Chamber of Commerce. Among the representatives were refugees who had escaped from the bandit-controlled areas, who painfully recounted their tragic experiences, with tears in their voices. The Chongqing press also hosted a banquet, and the two sides exchanged experiences. On February 2nd, they took a small boat north along the Jialing River, passing through Guanyin Gorge and arriving at Beibei. The clear waves and green hills were like a scene from springtime Jiangnan. Beibei is located between Libi Hot Springs, Guanyin, and the Three Gorges, and is a new village run by Lu Zuofu, Huang Zishang, and others. Ten years ago, it was a place haunted by bandits. Lu and others first formed a group to maintain security, and then cooperated with the residents to create various new enterprises, such as the Western China Academy of Sciences and the Institute of Physics and Chemistry, to engage in scientific exploration of the natural world in the west. In addition, there are the Jian Shan Middle School, the Civilian School, the Library (with 13,000 books), the Children's Library, the Civilian Hospital, the Public Sports Field, the Museum, and the Zoo. Although the various facilities are simple, they can maximize their function. There is also a very large Civilian Park for public recreation. In terms of productive enterprises, there is a dyeing and weaving factory that produces daily-use cloth. On the opposite bank of the river is the Beichuan Railway, which is only thirty li long and is used to transport coal from the mines to the docks, making a great contribution to the national economy and the people's livelihood. The Jialing Hotel is located above the hot spring gorge, inside the hot spring park, with an excellent environment. The waiters in the hotel are high school graduates aged fifteen or sixteen, called service students. They take care of everything for the travelers during the day, and at night they take turns guarding the night with live ammunition. Because the area is located in a secluded valley, there are often bandits, so residents must defend themselves. On the 4th, they boarded a ship from Beibei to return to Chongqing, and were scheduled to depart for Chengdu tomorrow morning. (Sent from Chongqing on the 5th)

Guangdong Province Unseals Frozen Rent

Frozen Rent Used to Maintain Finance

First Phase Matures, Unsealed and Interest Paid

Guangzhou Dispatch: Previously, due to the paper currency crisis in Guangdong Province, the government, under the pretext of maintaining finance and reducing the amount of paper currency in circulation in the market, announced that it would borrow one month's rent from shops and households in Guangzhou City, with tenants acting as agents for sealing it up. At that time, it was stipulated that the freeze period would be either two months or three months. Now that the two-month period has expired, the rent should be unsealed and interest paid. The first phase of borrowed rent is scheduled to be unsealed today (the 6th). The City Chamber of Commerce and the Elementary School Joint Association have been selected as the locations for the Guangdong Provincial Bank to unseal the rent and pay interest. The dates and methods for unsealing and paying interest are as follows: (1) The rent will be unsealed according to the number of days borrowed, averaged into two phases. The first phase is from December 6th, 22nd year to December 22nd of the same month, excluding weekly holidays, totaling fifteen days. Those who borrowed during this period will unseal after two months. The second phase is from December 23rd, 22nd year to January 13th, 23rd year, excluding weekly holidays, totaling sixteen days. Those who borrowed during this period will unseal after three months. (2) The unsealing of rent will be handled by an office organized by the Finance Department and the Provincial Bank. (3) The rent will be unsealed in the order of the borrowing date, and the bank will compile a table of unsealing dates and inform the public. (4) Those who have sealed up rent for shops should bring the original sealed rent to the office on the date specified in the announcement to have it verified and unsealed for interest payment. Those who do not arrive on time will have to wait until all the procedures are completed before they can proceed. They may not request a make-up on the day after the due date. (5) Interest on borrowed rent will be calculated at a monthly rate of eight per mille, and will be paid for either two months or three months. However, if the scheduled date exceeds two months or three months, the excess days will still be calculated for interest on a daily basis to ensure fairness. However, for those who do not come on time and delay until after all procedures are completed, interest will only be calculated up to the due date. The rent borrowing this time is based on the date of borrowing, the number of households sealed on that day, and the number of days to be processed. Because the first phase of borrowers was very enthusiastic, with as many as ten thousand households being sealed each day, and the number of sealed households in the second phase was very small, the procedures can be completed in a short period. The unsealing dates are divided into phases. For example, after the first phase is completed, the second phase will be compiled. The first unsealing dates are February 6th to 7th, February 8th to 13th, February 19th to 24th, and February 26th to March 6th. (February 6th)

Longxing Township Robbery Case Solved

The family of Chen Youquan, a villager from Xiaoqiujing, Tu 6, Longxing Bridge Township, north of Bailongtan in this city, was suddenly attacked by more than ten bandits at about 12 o'clock last night (the 8th). Suzhou

Carpenter and Painter Steal Hidden Gold

The Pan family of Baoji Bridge, Dongbaitazi Alley, Sucheng, has been a prominent family for generations, with considerable wealth. Their descendants Yonglin (third branch), Ruoshi (fourth branch), and Yongdong (fifth branch) separated and lived separately ten years ago, with a total of 1.8 million divided into five shares. Their old residence is deep and winding. It is said that when a concubine of the eldest branch died, because she had no descendants, she secretly buried cash and jewelry in the house, accumulating a considerable treasure. A certain painter in the east of the city, who owns considerable wealth, suddenly became rich several years ago. It is said that he found part of the hidden treasure while repairing the house. However, Yonglin and others had no evidence and let it go. Recently, about ten days ago, Zhu Asan, a carpenter regularly hired by the Pan family, and the painter Miao Zhiyun (who now runs the Miao Taicheng Lacquerware Store at No. 189 Lindun Road), were working at the residence when they suddenly discovered an official box in the ceiling. When they opened it, they were shocked to see a pile of gold and silver. They secretly carried it to Miao's store, where they weighed it and found one hundred taels of gold arhats and other pure gold, two hundred Japanese gold coins, and four hundred and ten silver dollars. They immediately split it up. Miao got eighty taels of pure gold, Zhu got twenty taels, and they split the remaining items in half. Afterwards, a apprentice in Miao's store found out and gradually leaked it out. Miao had no choice but to confess to the Pan family. The Pan family then filed a request with the Public Security Bureau, ordering the Mudu Branch Bureau to send police to Zhu Asan's home in Xiangshan, arrest Zhu in the city, and recover the stolen gold that Zhu had deposited at No. 4 Pingjiang Road. On the 8th, Pan Yonglin and others lured Miao Zhiyun to the Public Security Bureau and had him arrested. It is said that at the time when the concubine buried the gold, there was also a booklet in the official box, which noted all the gold and silver buried in various places. To clarify the total amount of hidden treasure, the first step is to track down this booklet. In the evening, after a secret interrogation by the Public Security Bureau, Miao Zhiyun, Zhu Asan, and Jin Nan, an apprentice at Miao's store, confessed that they had indeed weighed and divided the stolen gold and other items at Miao's store. The three were sent back to prison. On the evening of the 8th, a detective team, together with the police station in charge, raided Miao's store. This incident caused a sensation in society. It is said that after Miao received the stolen gold, he put part of it in a chamber pot. Later, when Miao confessed, he had two buckets transported to Ruoshi, a member of the Pan clan. This was seen by a night watchman at the Zhixiang pawnshop nearby, so there was also some infighting among the Pan clan.

Huinan

Small Carpenter Chops Paramour to Death

Cheng Jinxiang, who is from Nanshi Shao of Datuan Town in the fifth district, has been having an affair with Xia, the wife of Chen Aqiu, a small carpenter. Because Chen is addicted to morphine injections and lives in poverty, he uses this to supplement his income, so he knowingly ignores the affair between Chen and Xia. However, Cheng is quite stingy. For many years, he has not spent much. Recently, Chen, because the end of the lunar year was approaching and he could not repay his debts, gathered a person the night before last, and when Cheng was secretly meeting with Xia, they broke down the door and tied up Cheng with a rope, demanding fifty yuan. Because Cheng refused, Chen stabbed Cheng's leg three times with an awl. Although blood flowed freely, Cheng still refused. Chen became extremely angry and chopped Cheng's head with an axe, immediately splitting his eyes and nose. Cheng died instantly. Chen and others, seeing that they had caused trouble, transported Cheng's body to the side of the road in Fengxian. Yesterday morning, the body was discovered and reported to the district office and public security bureau of the town for inspection. The murderer was arrested and a flannel blood-stained shirt, as well as an axe and iron awl with blood stains, were found in his home. A floor with blood stains was also found in front of the bed. All were sent to the county for interrogation.

Aunt Killing Case Opens for Interrogation

Chen Wang, the wife of Chen Baogen, the owner of the Chen Tingji woodworking shop in Lixiang, outside the West Gate, was chopped three times with an axe in the middle of the night on the 26th of last month by her nephew Feng AqI, Chen Qibao, and her own daughter, Chen Cuiyun. Her brain matter splattered and she died immediately. The Fourth Branch of the Public Security Bureau arrested the murderers and sent them to the court. After repeated interrogations, Qibao confessed to having an affair with Cuiyun and being discovered by his aunt, leading him to kill her out of resentment. Later, he suddenly retracted his confession. Yesterday, the prosecutor from the Prosecutor's Office summoned Chen Baogen, the husband of the deceased, to court for questioning. According to his testimony, the key points in the case are: (1) Several days before the incident, Qibao borrowed a handgun from his friend. When his friend asked what it was for, he said he was going out to start a business. Qibao was silent, but the gun was not borrowed. (2) On the day of the incident, after ten o'clock at night, Qibao opened the door and went out. When asked what he was doing, he said he was urinating. The witness said that there was a chamber pot for urination, so why go out? Qibao then changed his story and said he was defecating. A few hours later, Wang was hacked to death. The prosecutor considered the above two points to be of great importance, and continued to question Qibao for a long time before ordering him to be returned to prison. Chen Baogen was ordered to return home.

Resolutions of the Party and Government Meeting

The county government of this county convened the seventh Party and government meeting at ten o'clock on the morning of the 9th, chaired by Yan Shenyu. Items for discussion: (1) The gambling trend in urban and rural areas has not been curbed recently. It is currently the end of the lunar year, and the customs are particularly deep. Strict prohibition should be enforced. The case was decided: (A) The county government will issue a notice to reiterate the strict prohibition of gambling. (B) The Public Security Bureau will order each branch bureau to be responsible for the effective implementation. (C) The county government will order each district office to jointly inspect with each public security branch bureau. (D) The Party Department will order each lower-level Party department to conduct strict investigation and report at any time. (E) Anyone who knows the location of gambling places may report the true situation to the county government or the Public Security Bureau for investigation, but may not make false accusations out of malice. (F) In the future, gambling cases will be seized, gambling places will be sealed by the Public Security Bureau, and gamblers and those who collect fees to gather gamblers will be sent to the court for strict investigation. (2) Recently, the labor groups have shown signs of decline, and factories often ignore the labor unions. Urgent rescue should be carried out. The case was decided to be referred by the county government to the Chamber of Commerce, which will inform the factories to pay attention to the Labor Union Law and to provide guidance to labor groups.

Prosecutor Investigates the Case of Falsely Accusing Good People of Theft

The case of Jin Jishan, the former director of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau, falsely accusing Li Shouqi, a good citizen, of theft, and torturing him to death, has been investigated and concluded by the county government. It was ruled that Patrolman Huang Tianjia and Gatekeeper Cao Jiapin, jointly abused the power and opportunity of their positions to injure others. Each was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and one year of deprivation of civil rights. Jin Jishan is at large, and the trial will be suspended in order. Li Yu's widow believed that the ruling was inappropriate since the main culprit was still at large, and the injustice had not been redressed, she appealed to the Shanghai Local Court. City News

Ministry of Communications Prepares for International Wireless Telephone

Has Successfully Tested with England, America, France, and Germany

After Success, Machines Will Be Purchased for Formal Calls

Huadong News Agency reports: Since the Ministry of Communications successfully established direct wireless communication with England, it has been preparing for further convenience and is planning to implement mutual wireless telephone communication with European countries. Tests are currently underway and have been conducted with Germany, the United States, and England, with excellent results. A long-term test is planned, and after its success, a wireless telephone machine will be purchased from a foreign country specifically for formal communication with other countries.

Test Calls with Various Countries

After the establishment of direct central international wireless communication, the Ministry of Communications immediately ordered the International Telecommunications Bureau, in its spare time from Sino-British communication, to still use the Sino-British radio station to conduct mutual wireless telephone communication, so that clear language can be heard from thousands of miles away. This matter has been worked hard by the Bureau, and communication is possible with excellent results. Initially, the Bureau conducted a test call with the wireless radio station in Berlin, Germany, using clear and gentle German. Later, Liu Chongjie, the ambassador to Germany, and Liu Hongsheng, the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, talked to each other for a long time. The other day, the station invited the German Ruituo from Siemens in this city to hold a call with Berlin, Germany. The Berlin radio station was relayed to the small city of Düssqfdort, 500 miles away from Berlin, and it was able to obtain good sound waves, as if it were right in front of you. After obtaining this result, the station held calls with London, England, and New York, USA, and the results were also good. It is now planned to carry out calls with Paris, the capital of France.

Continued Research

After the International Telecommunications Bureau successfully tested calls with various countries, it believed that although the results of this call were good, it was not yet fully confident, so it continued to research and planned to conduct test calls with various countries again using the Sino-British wireless radio station. However, the station has been very busy recently and has very few free times, so it can only hold test calls for a few hours each week, so it is difficult to determine when it can be completely successful.

Purchasing Telephones

After the Bureau successfully conducted wireless telephone trials with various countries, it will soon formally accept commercial telegrams. However, due to the current heavy workload of the machinery, it is unable to spare time to receive and transmit telephone calls. Therefore, it plans to purchase another wireless telephone machine from abroad in the near future, specifically for telephone communication with various countries. When successful in the future, we will be able to converse with acquaintances thousands of miles away.
