Central Mint Held a Standing Committee Meeting for Review Yesterday

Secretariat Reported on Work

Assayer Reported on Review Process

The Central Mint Review Committee held its tenth standing committee meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday in the auditorium on the third floor of the Central Bank, chaired by Kong Xiangxi. The Secretariat and the Assayer reported on their work. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. Details are as follows:

Committee Members Present

The following committee members were present: Kong Yongzhi, Bei Songsun, Wu Yunzhai, Hu Mengjia, Shi Demen, Ye Zhuotang, Shi Taijin, Shi Huang, Tai Wei, Lin Shu, Dai Jingfu, Qin Runqing, Xu Jichu, Chen Guangfu, Lai Aisi, Hao Shumin, Li Ming, Geng Aide, Xue Laiden, Mai Kai, Ma Xier, Chen Zheqing, Hu Yunzhuang, Xi Demao, Lai Na, and others. Committee members Chen Jian'an was absent due to leave. The following attended as observers: Lu Jianquan, Director of the Mint; Wei Jingzhou, Deputy Director; Wei Tingtao, Section Chief; Qiao Furen, Secretary; and Ge Laide, Assayer.

Secretary's Report

Secretary Qiao Furen reported: (1) This year, in January, 4,400,000 yuan of legal new currency was reviewed and deemed legitimate. In addition, the inspection of 65 Class A factory bars (999 fineness) and 2,730 Class B factory bars (880 fineness) with additional stamps have been approved for release from the factory. In addition to being listed in public notices, the Ministry of Finance has been informed with a letter, requesting that the drafts and forms of the announcements be published in the "Finance Daily." (2) The Ministry of Finance previously sent two documents for receiving funds, requesting that the expenses of this committee be filled out separately by month according to the attached list. This has been done on the 9th of this month and sent to the Ministry. (3) The Ministry of Finance has replied to the committee's work report for November of last year, approving it for record. However, the original letter stated that the review of the factory's silver account forms would have to wait until the factory submits them to the Ministry separately before a comprehensive review could be conducted. (4) The Ministry of Finance approved the committee's letter of January 6 regarding the review of legal new currency and the number of stamped factory bars for December of the 22nd year and the announcement drafts and forms, replying on January 18 that they have been filed separately and published in the "Finance Daily." (5) The committee's voucher for February's regular expenses has been sent to the Ministry in accordance with regulations on the 15th of this month. (6) The work report for December of the 22nd year on the committee's review of new currency, the number of stamped factory bars, and the handling of committee affairs has now been compiled and sent to the Ministry of Finance. The accounting section's forms for December of the Central Mint have not yet been sent to the committee. According to the accounting department of the factory, they are currently processing the year-end final accounts and will send them for review as soon as they are completed. Furthermore, the accounting and expenditure situation will be reported at the next general meeting after the factory sends the forms for review.

Casting Report

The factory has submitted for verification a report on the melting of silver ingots for December, a report on the melting of factory bars, weekly reports on Class A and Class B factory bars, weekly casting report forms, and silver receipts and disbursements report forms. After reviewing the factory's books in accordance with the items listed in the forms, the following is a brief description of the accounts: (1) Factory bars cast into new currency: According to the investigation, the factory cast new currency for 25 days in December, casting a total of 4,712,690 yuan of new currency, with an average of 188,507 yuan per day. 4,750,000 yuan were transferred to the Central Bank, which is consistent with the number of qualified products reviewed by the committee in December. In addition, 1,133 Class 999 factory bars and 227 Class 880 factory bars were cast in December, which is consistent with the number stamped by the committee. According to this year's statistics from the date of opening the mint to the end of December, a total of 28,060,926 yuan of silver coins were cast, of which 27,670,000 yuan were transferred to the Central Bank (including 2,260,000 yuan of old molds), 3,556 Class 999 factory bars, of which 3,550 were transferred to the Central Bank, and 227 Class 880 factory bars, of which 20 were transferred to the Central Bank. These have been combined and noted. (2) Name of silver used and amount of copper: According to the silver ingot melting report (regarding the melting of one-yuan silver) sent by the factory daily, there were a total of 25 reports, indicating that the net weight of silver melted in December was 10,810,388.01 ounces, and the weight of copper was 1,479,579.23 ounces. In percentage terms, the silver content accounted for 87.96%, and the copper content accounted for 12.04%. According to the Class B factory bar melting report, there were a total of eight reports, indicating that the net weight of silver melted in December was 777,082.70 ounces, and the total weight of copper was 106,041.53 ounces. In percentage terms, the silver content accounted for 87.994%, and the copper content accounted for 12.006%. The quantity of silver used for Class 999 factory bars will be reported at the general meeting next month and combined for statement.

Assay Report

Assayer Ge Laide reported that the Central Mint cast a total of 4.4 million yuan of new currency in January. In compliance with regulations, 490 yuan were randomly selected for public assay. The average fineness was 880.35, which is 0.35 higher than the statutory standard. The weight was 26.689080 fen, which is 3/10000 lower than the statutory weight, both within the statutory tolerance. In addition, the 65 Class A factory bars of 999 fineness and the 2,730 Class B factory bars of 880 fineness that passed the review in the same month were also supervised by the Assayer and stamped with the committee's seal when marking the benchmark, in accordance with regulations.

And Seek Joint Development in Business

The Special Municipal Party Department and the Bureau of Social Affairs of this city issued a joint announcement yesterday, stating that, "Regarding the matter of joint announcement, the end of January is approaching, which is the time for businesses to finalize their accounts. Employers in various industries often take advantage of ingrained practices to dismiss workers under various pretexts, causing them to suffer the pain of unemployment. This not only leads to disputes but is also prohibited by laws and regulations. China's Tung Oil Exports Increased Significantly Last Year

A Quarter More Than in the 21st Year of the Republic of China

Most Widely Used in the United States, Britain, and Hong Kong

According to the International Trade Bureau yesterday, Tung oil is one of China's special products and an indispensable raw material for the paint manufacturing industry. It is mostly produced in Sichuan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and the Yangtze River area. The largest market is Hankou, with annual exports of over one million dan, worth approximately tens of millions of national currency. The United States accounts for approximately 70% of the total exports. Other countries such as Britain, Germany, France, the Netherlands, and Japan also import it. In recent years, the United States Department of Agriculture has been studying the planting of Tung trees carefully. Since 1913, trials have been conducted. As of 1933, the planting area occupied approximately 40,000 acres, with approximately 4 million Tung trees. China is the earliest country to produce Tung oil. If there is no organization to improve matters, it is feared that it will follow in the footsteps of silk and tea and fall behind. The statistics on China's Tung oil exports to various countries over the past two years are as follows:

Increase in Exports to the United States Last Year

Trade Statistics to the United States in January of This Year

According to the Great American Evening News, the statistics compiled by the U.S. Consulate General in Shanghai based on the manifests issued by the consulate in January of this year show that the total value of goods shipped from Shanghai to the United States was US$1,190,291. Inedible animals and animal products ranked first, accounting for $766,117, of which gray squirrels accounted for $398,361. Textiles ranked second, valued at $366,260. Various straw hat materials ranked third, valued at $130,023. Linen embroidery ranked fourth, valued at $102,902. Vegetables, food, and beverages ranked fifth, valued at $32,757. The remaining miscellaneous goods ranged from several thousand to several hundred dollars each. The total value of goods shipped from Shanghai to the Philippine Islands this month was US$136,071. Various cotton products ranked first, valued at $29,851. Machine oil and grease ranked second, valued at $24,888. Cotton yarn ranked third, valued at $23,412. Ham was $13,477 and beans were $10,656. The value of all other goods was less than 10,000. The total value of goods shipped from Shanghai to Hawaii this month was US$4,623, of which woodenware accounted for $1,189.

According to the U.S. Consulate General in Shanghai, the total value of goods shipped from China to the United States in 1933 was US$34,242,179, an increase of $7,947,327 compared to 1932. In that year, all categories except five saw an increase. The largest increase was in textiles, which jumped from $7,797,010 to $11,503,586, an increase of $3,706,576. Inedible animals and animal products, including raw hides and leather goods, and other animal products, were worth $11,707,070, compared to $8,633,926 in 1932. Textiles were the second largest increase, an increase of $3,706,576 compared to 1932. The total value of inedible vegetable products (excluding textiles and wood) also increased significantly, with a total value of $6,481,320 in 1933, compared to only $4,457,241 in 1932. Vegetables, food, and beverages ranked fourth, with a total value of $2,081,166, compared to $1,851,300 in 1932. Exports of edible animals and animal products decreased slightly this year. Tea was worth $967,584, compared to $1,405,024 in 1932. The largest decrease was in the category of metals and manufactured products (excluding machinery and vehicles). The total value of exports in 1932 was $1,255,262, which fell to $702,720 in 1933, a decrease of $552,542. Wood and paper also saw a decrease, with $77,991 in 1933, compared to $183,082 in 1932. The increase or decrease of other exported items varied. Non-metallic minerals were worth $460,980 ($194,282 in 1932), machinery and vehicles were worth $2,453 ($706 in 1932), and chemicals and related chemical products were worth $155,089 ($432,798 in 1932).

Record of the General Meeting of Chinese Tobacco Industry

Twenty-Four Companies Request Improvement of Tax Rate

Huang Ziping Talks About United Support for Small Factories

The Chinese Cigarette Industry Association held a supplementary meeting of its third membership meeting at the Central Western Restaurant on Sima Road at 3:00 PM yesterday. Representatives from the following factories attended: Li Xing Gengsheng, Da Dong Qiu Tanglin, Da Dong Sun Lishan, Hua Xing Hu Ruiting, Hua Min Shen Xingde, Da Zhonghua Chen Dejiao, Yazhou Peng Zizhen, Min Zhong Huang Ziping, Jinsha Zhou Tingzi, and 29 other factories, as well as more than ten attending members. Representatives from the Municipal Party Department He Yuanming, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Yuan Hongjun, the Tax Bureau Jiang Chengyi, and the Tax Bureau of the Jiangsu-Anhui District Chen Yan attended to provide guidance. Bao Gengsheng chaired the meeting, and Wu Peiyin recorded the minutes. The meeting began as scheduled. The chairman's report was omitted. Matters for discussion: (1) The case of the request from Min Zhong and 24 other companies to improve the tax rate: First, Huang Ziping, the representative of the Min Zhong Company, reported on the proposal. Next, the chairman stated that the previous resolution was to publicly elect Huang Ziping, Bao Gengsheng, Lao Jingxiu, Shen Xingde, Zhao Shao, Chen Maonan, Zhang Xinliang, Jing Yimeng, and Ding Boquan, nine people in total, to review the proposal and then submit it to the Executive Committee for processing. Resolution: Passed. (2) The Ministry of Finance agreed to allocate 300,000 foreign dollars to develop Chinese businesses and improve tobacco leaf. First, the chairman explained the resolution of the previous discussion meeting, stating that the funds would be kept by the industry association and should be acknowledged as such. Resolution: Passed. Next, nine people were publicly elected as custodians: Dai Gengxin, Ding Boquan, Huang Ziping, Lao Jingxiu, Bao Gengsheng, Zhao Yunshao, Zhang Xinliang, Jing Yimeng, and Shen Xingde were publicly elected as custodians. As for the use of the funds, it is limited to assisting in anti-smuggling, improving tobacco leaves, and constructing association facilities. Resolution: Passed. The meeting adjourned at approximately 5:00 PM.

A reporter from the Guowen News Agency met with Mr. Huang Ziping after the meeting. According to him, Chinese businesses have been greatly affected since the seven-level tax was changed to a three-level tax. There were originally 150 or 160 Chinese businesses under the seven-level tax, but after the tax was changed again to a two-level tax, factories closed down one after another, leaving only 40 or 50. If no measures are taken to remedy the situation urgently, then in a few years, Chinese cigarette factories will be completely forced to close down. Also, this tax change favors high-grade cigarettes. Before they were aware of this, large Chinese factories made no representation. Now, large factories such as Nanyang have expressed unanimous support for small factories, and Nanyang has also issued a separate declaration, which roughly states: "Upon investigation, the 24 cigarette factories, including Min Zhong, believe that the current cigarette tax rate heavily taxes low-grade cigarettes and lightly taxes high-grade cigarettes, resulting in unequal treatment. A case has been submitted to the government requesting improvement. The Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance has sent a letter to the Shanghai Cigarette Factory Industry Association for review. After discussions at the Association's meeting, it was resolved that members should express their opinions as much as possible. Since cigarettes flowed into China, money has flowed out by the tens of millions each year. Our industry has been operating diligently, only slightly plugging the leaks. Our government has spared no effort in protecting and promoting domestic industries in recent years. Although cigarettes are luxury goods, they are still an industry. Even if protective tariffs cannot be implemented, at least equal treatment should be given so that Chinese businesses can compete with foreign businesses. Our company is also a Chinese business, and fortunately, it has some high-grade cigarette production, which benefits somewhat. However, it is unbearable to sit and watch the decline of fellow businesses. Moreover, low taxes on high-grade cigarettes increase sales, while high taxes on low-grade cigarettes cause sales to stagnate. The tobacco leaves for low-grade cigarettes are all domestically produced, and if this leads to stagnation, then the livelihoods of farmers will be cut off. How can we bear to sit and watch the starvation of farmers in several provinces and ignore it? Our company has not been listed in the original proposal of Min Zhong and others, but we have sympathy. Our government is currently busy with military affairs and the agricultural sector is facing difficulties, and funds were hastily raised without considering this temporary unfair tax rate, which is not the original intention of our government to promote and protect industry. After our colleagues earnestly submit their appeal, we believe it will be accepted. As for the industry's suggestions for tax reform, the more levels, the more burdens, otherwise, taxation based on price is the fairest. It is said that the country is rich and the people are not exhausted, the tax is high but the rate is not harsh."

Joint Meeting of Charities Resolves to Request Exemption from Property Land Tax

Deadline for Filling Out and Reporting Forms Within Two Weeks

According to the Guomin News Agency, the Shanghai Federation of Charitable Organizations convened a joint meeting of representatives from various charitable organizations at its office on Yunnan Road at 4:00 PM yesterday. Representatives from over twenty organizations attended.

Representatives Attending the Meeting

Representatives attending the meeting included Wang Zhongfu of the Guangyi Benevolent Hall, Wang Zhongfu of the China Relief for Women and Children, Fei Jintang of the Wei Zhong Benevolent Hall, Weng Yinchu of the Lanyi Benevolent Association, Ye Shouhai of the Xin Puyu Hall, Chen Wenkui of the Shanghai Disabled Persons' Home, He Songshou of the Tongyi Benevolent Association, Sun Yishan of the Hunan Charitable Association, Liu Zuojun of the Shanghai Jixin Association, Wu Shutian of the Shanghai Charitable Group, Zhou Chuliang of the Public Shanghai Hospital, Gu Xizhou of the Gongji Hall, Gu Xizhou of the Fushan Hall, Wang Shenfu of the Horen Hall, Zhang Xianqing of the China Jisheng Association, Ni Rongtai of the Zhan Industry Public Righteousness Association, Luo Xingyou of the Zhabei Charitable Group, Zhang Junkang of the Shanghai Orphanage, Fang Zhijun of the Renji Benevolent Hall, Tai Yanqi of the Shanghai Charitable Group, Chen

Page 14

Shufeng of the Renji Nursery, Huang Hanzhi of the Xinwei Relief Association, and Wang Yiting, and other representatives from twenty-two organizations, totaling twenty-three people. Huang Hanzhi was publicly elected as chairman. The meeting began as scheduled.

Chairman's Report

The chairman began by stating that the city is currently levying land value tax, starting with the areas of Hunan, Zhabei, and Pudong. The amount of the levy is often ten to dozens of times higher than the original levies. According to Article 2 of the Land Tax Levy Regulations, land used for public charitable purposes without income may be exempted from the temporary land value tax upon approval by the Municipal Government. Therefore, the office locations and charitable graveyards of various charitable organizations, which do not generate income, can apply for exemption. How to deal with the remaining income-generating land should be discussed in detail.

Resolutions

The income from land constitutes the majority of the funding for charitable organizations' charitable activities. In recent years, the market has declined, and rural areas have gone bankrupt. Income has already been sharply reduced, while the number of impoverished people has increased daily, making it necessary to find ways to provide relief, and expenses have actually increased. Adding a huge land tax would be an unbearable burden. All office locations and charitable graveyards of various charitable organizations without income should naturally apply for exemption in accordance with regulations. The remaining income-generating land should also be petitioned for reduction in order to maintain operations. The association will draft a form to notify various charitable organizations to list all land within the currently taxed areas, separating them into income-generating and non-income-generating categories, and report them to the association within two weeks so that they can be compiled and submitted for reduction or exemption. The meeting adjourned at approximately 7:00 PM.

No Expansion of Taxed Business Districts for Land Value Tax Collection

According to the Central News Agency, since the land value tax was implemented in this city, although some landlords have repeatedly requested postponement or exemption, the municipal authorities believe that the situation in this city is different from that in the interior, and that the tax collection had already started in the concessions. The tax rate set this time in the Chinese-controlled area is also lower than that in the concessions, so it is not convenient to change it. Since its implementation, progress has been smooth. As for the rumor that the taxed business districts for the temporary land value tax collection will be expanded, according to sources from the Land Bureau, there is no such intention. Expanding business districts would require consideration of the market situation and submission to the central government for approval before it could be implemented. Therefore, the rumor is not accurate.

Rent Reduction Movement in Various Districts

No Panic Withdrawals at Guangdong Postal Savings

Postal Savings Bureau Received Telegram

Central News Agency reports that regarding rumors of panic withdrawals at the Guangzhou Post Office Savings Bank for several consecutive days, reporters visited the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau yesterday for inquiries. According to Xu Yuanfang, the director of the General Affairs Department of the bureau, the bureau had telegraphed the Guangzhou branch to inquire about this matter and had received a reply stating that there were no panic withdrawals. However, as it was approaching the end of the abolished lunar year, the general public, whose customs had not changed, were withdrawing more savings to meet their needs, hence the increase in the number of withdrawals at the bureau in recent days. Xu continued to say that the situation was generally the same everywhere every year, so the so-called panic withdrawals were not true.

Additional Third and Fourth Class Shanghai-Wuxi Trains Added to Beijing-Shanghai Railway

From Today Until the 13th

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Traffic Department, in light of the abolished lunar new year and the fact that many people from various places in Shanghai were returning to their hometowns for the holidays, especially those from the middle and lower classes, which resulted in insufficient capacity on the existing third and fourth class trains, specially added one round-trip third and fourth class train between Shanghai and Wuxi starting from the 8th of this month. Since passenger volume remains extremely congested, the railway authorities, to facilitate passenger travel, have decided to add another third and fourth class train between Shanghai North Station and Wuxi from the 10th to the 13th of this month, with intermediate stops at Kunshan and Suzhou stations. The timetable is recorded as follows: Shanghai North Station departure: 12:30 AM; Kunshan arrival: 1:41 AM, departure: 1:44 AM; Suzhou arrival: 2:32 AM, departure: 2:42 AM; Wuxi arrival: 3:47 AM.

Rice Market Closed for Spring Festival Trading Starting Yesterday

Reopening Date to Be Decided by the General Meeting

City's Total Grain Reserves Estimated at Over One Million Piculs

This month's 13th is the closing date for the Spring Festival. The city's north and south rice markets will be closed for trading starting yesterday. After unloading their cargo, all rice boats will return to their hometowns for the holidays. The total amount of grain stored in the city's various businesses and factories is estimated to be over one million piculs. The details are recorded below:

Suspension of Trading

The Shanghai Bean and Rice Trade Association held an ad-hoc meeting of the rice group at Cuixiu Hall at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, deciding that from the 9th of this month (i.e., yesterday), the 23rd year's Spring Festival would be the final closing period, and all trading would be suspended. The official reopening date would be decided at a general meeting of all businesses on the 18th.

Rice Boats Departing

The Wuxi, Kunshan, Changshu, Jiaozhi, Qingpu, Zhujiajiao, Tongli, Songjiang, Chongming, Gaoyou, Shaobo, Pingwang, and other local rice boats docked at the north and south rice industry wharves have unloaded their cargo in recent days and, after settling their accounts, have departed for their hometowns for the holidays the day before yesterday. The first batch of cargo to arrive in Shanghai is expected around the 20th of this month.

Business Profits and Losses

A reporter from Dagong News visited Zhu Zixiang, a standing committee member of the Bean and Rice Trade Association, yesterday to inquire about the business profits and losses of various businesses and factories in the 22nd year. According to Zhu, due to the accumulation of inventory, the sharp drop in rice prices, and the impact of the current situation and tight finances, all 29 businesses in the industry suffered losses. Even those with profits earned very little. These are the general conditions. The detailed total profits and losses will be announced after the final settlement.

Gu Xinyi and Bian Xiaoqing Petition the Ministry of Finance to Issue Flour and Wheat Purchase Price Deduction Vouchers

If Calculated According to World Prices, Manufacturers Will Suffer Great Losses

Hoping That the Initial Intent to Benefit Merchants Will Be Quickly Adopted to Seek Relief Measures

Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Shanghai Flour Mill Industry Association, and Bian Xiaoqing, Chairman of the Su, Zhe, and Anhui Inland Flour Mill Industry Association, recently noted that the Ministry of Finance's Cotton and Wheat Management Office is calculating the purchase price of flour and wheat for manufacturers according to world prices, which differ greatly from domestic market prices. They specially petitioned Kong Xiangxi, the Minister of Finance, requesting the Ministry of Finance to issue flour and wheat purchase price deduction vouchers to be deducted proportionally, in order to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. The original petition is recorded as follows: "Petitioning Regarding the Immediate Collection of the Announced Import Tax on Foreign Wheat, Causing Unexpected Losses for Manufacturers That Are Difficult to Bear. We Again Urgently Request Reimbursement According to the Amount, to Alleviate Merchants' Difficulties and Maintain Industry. We Humbly Submit That We Previously Petitioned to Request Exemption from Wheat Tax on the Foreign Wheat Import Tariffs Set by Various Manufacturers Before the Tax Announcement. We Were Grateful That Your Excellency Allowed Our Association's Various Factories to Purchase American Flour and Wheat Lent by the Government and, Within the Payment Due, to Deduct 5% of the Loss of Previously Paid Foreign Wheat Import Tariffs. We Reverently Acknowledge That Your Excellency Has Insightfully Recognized the Difficulties of Manufacturers and Provided Comprehensive Protection. All Members of the Industry Are Overwhelmed With Gratitude and Dare Not Raise Any Further Objections. However, the Process of Negotiating the Purchase of Flour and Wheat Has Resulted in Facts That Were Not Originally Envisioned or Expected by Your Excellency, and We Must Once Again Express Our Sentiments to the Minister. Manufacturers Followed the Minister's Order, Dispatching Representatives to Confer With the Cotton and Wheat Management Office Regarding the Terms of Purchase of Flour and Wheat. Over the Course of Several Weeks, the Main Condition, the Price, Proved Impossible for Manufacturers to Accept. The Cotton and Wheat Management Office Instructed Manufacturers to Purchase at World Prices, Which Differ Greatly From Domestic Market Prices. If Manufacturers Purchased Flour and Wheat at World Prices, Not Only Would They Be Unable to Offset the Loss of Previously Paid Tariffs, but They Would Also Be Burdened With Losses Several Times Greater Than the Tariffs. The Cotton and Wheat Management Office Is Unable to Uphold Your Excellency's Generous Intention to Protect Manufacturers. Therefore, the Terms of Purchase of Flour and Wheat Were Ultimately Difficult to Sign. Manufacturers Have Already Paid the Foreign Wheat Import Tariffs and Can Only Continue to Beseech Your Excellency to Maintain the Original Intention of Benefiting Merchants in Difficulty and Rescuing Industry, To Approve, Under the Name of Encouragement or Relief, the Issuance of Flour and Wheat Purchase Price Deduction Vouchers According to the Amount of the Previously Paid Wheat Tax by Each Factory, Which Should Be Handed Over to Those Factories, Allowing Them to Proportionally Deduct From the Payments Due For the Repurchase of Government-Lent Flour and Wheat. This Method Benefits Both Sides, Upholding the Credibility of Your Ministry's Order From Above and Preventing the Crumbling Flour Industry From Going Bankrupt. Your Excellency's Intention to Benefit Merchants in Difficulty and Rescue Industry Would Also Be Further Highlighted. If Approved, Not Only Would Our Association's Various Factories Feel the Grateful Protection, But the Livelihoods of Tens of Thousands of Workers and the Revenue of National Taxes and Unified Taxes Could Also Be Spared. We Urgently Express Our Sentiments and Humbly Await Your Orders. Respectfully Submitted."

Gu Xinyi Telegraphs to Guangdong Authorities Requesting the Cancellation of Special Tax on Domestic Oil Beans

Imposing Taxes on Imported Agricultural Products Was Originally Intended to Protect Farmers and Merchants

Now Taxing Domestic Products Will Only Accelerate the Collapse of Agriculture

Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oilcake Trade Association, yesterday telegraphed the Executive Committee of the Southwest Political Conference of Guangzhou, the Guangdong Provincial Government, the Provincial and Municipal Party Committees, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating: (Omissions) According to industry reports, the Guangdong Province has established a special tax bureau for imported agricultural products, levying special taxes on imported agricultural products. However, recently, domestically produced peanuts, soybeans, and crude oil transported to Guangdong have been detained by the bureau. In recent years, farmers and merchants have been in dire straits, reaching their limit. The establishment of a bureau to levy special taxes on imported goods was originally intended to protect farmers and merchants, and the bureau should focus on taxing foreign goods to avoid contradicting the original purpose. Now, taxing domestic products will only accelerate the collapse of farmers and merchants. Furthermore, the Guangdong Provincial Department of Finance has announced that wheat bran is subject to surcharges, and peanuts, soybeans, and crude oil, which are related to people's food, are even more important, so taxing them together with imported products is not a fair practice. We humbly request that this special tax be immediately abolished. The telegram is urgently dispatched. Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oilcake Trade Association.

Shanghai Social Bureau Provides Relief to Disaster Areas

Appealing for Sponsorship From Philanthropists

The Shanghai Social Bureau has always paid close attention to handling charitable affairs. Since the January 28th Incident two years ago, the disaster-stricken areas of the city have covered an area of more than 140 hectares, with a population of more than 600,000. The bureau has raised funds to organize various loan relief and other relief activities, benefiting the people greatly and achieving significant results. However, due to the large size of the disaster area and the large number of disaster victims, the previously raised funds were still insufficient for application. The bureau has continued to organize relief efforts in the war zone. In addition to government allocations, it plans to raise donations from Chinese and foreign philanthropists in order to ensure that relief efforts are widespread. A reporter from the Central News Agency specially inquired about this matter with Wu Huanru, the section chief of the Second Section of the Shanghai Social Bureau. According to Wu, in recent times, the city has not yet recovered from the old wounds of the January 28th Incident, farmers have suffered from natural disasters last year, and the commercial environment is extremely desolate. The people's suffering is difficult to describe in words. Several groups come to the bureau every day to request relief. The bureau's responsibility lies in trying its best to find ways to provide relief. Although the bureau currently has 20,000 to 30,000 yuan in cash donated by various sectors, it is merely a drop in the bucket. In order to ensure widespread relief, it is planned to appeal to Chinese and foreign philanthropists to remember the suffering of the disaster victims and generously donate. However, in order to avoid the emergence of malpractices, the bureau is only soliciting donations through newspaper advertisements. Anyone willing to donate should send the donations to the Shanghai Municipal Bank and notify the bureau. Once a certain amount has been collected, the bureau will start organizing various relief activities. As for the methods of organizing, they will be determined based on the future fundraising situation.

A Coal Train on the Jinpu Railway Derailed in Chuzhou

Traffic Disruption on the Ping-Hu Line

Incident Occurred the Day Before Yesterday, Repaired at 8 PM That Evening

Through Train From Ping Arrived Only This Morning

A coal train on the Jinpu Railway derailed at Chuzhou Station the day before yesterday, disrupting both passenger and freight trains. Through service train No. 301 from Ping to Shanghai was delayed and arrived in Shanghai only at 7:00 AM this morning. The details are recorded below:

Coal Train Derailed: A coal train on the Jinpu Railway derailed near Chuzhou Station at around 11:00 AM the day before yesterday due to damage to the tracks. Fortunately, the driver immediately noticed and stopped the train. All the coal cars attached were not derailed, only the locomotive overturned. The Jinpu Railway Bureau dispatched a rescue train from the engineering department to the accident site to lift the overturned locomotive and repair the damaged track sleepers. Repairs were completed and traffic was restored at 8:00 PM that evening.

Traffic Restored: Through service train No. 301 from Ping to Shanghai, which arrived at Chuzhou Station at 1:30 PM the day before yesterday, and through service train No. 302 from Shanghai to Ping, which arrived at Chuzhou Station at 12:15 PM the day before yesterday, were both disrupted due to the damaged tracks. At the same time, the fourth Puzhen express train on the Jinpu Railway, which arrived at Chuzhou Station at 11:30 AM the day before yesterday, was also disrupted. After repairs were completed at 8:00 PM, traffic was restored. Through service train No. 301 from Ping to Shanghai was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 11:55 PM the night before yesterday but was delayed and arrived in Shanghai at 7:10 AM this morning.

Uniform Time for Raising the National Flag at Various Agencies

The Municipal Public Security Bureau received an instruction from the Municipal Government yesterday, stating that the time for raising the national flag at various agencies under the jurisdiction of the city was inconsistent, which was disrespectful. It has now been stipulated that all agencies under the jurisdiction of the city should uniformly raise the national flag at 8:30 AM every day and lower it at 8:30 PM. You are to comply with this order. In addition to issuing a general order, you are hereby ordered to instruct all district police stations and teams under your jurisdiction to comply with this order uniformly.

Dyeing Industry Association Held a Closing Meeting Yesterday

Adopting a Spirit of Unity

Determining Methods to Deal With Individual Breaches

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Association held an emergency meeting yesterday to discuss various issues related to the closing period for the current term and the settlement of accounts for the industry. The following resolutions were made: (1) Regarding how to settle accounts: It was resolved that, during the current closing period, members should settle dyeing accounts with silk shops collectively with colleagues from the heji tou industry, starting from February 9th. If a member settles accounts individually, that member will be held fully responsible for compensating for any losses suffered by the industry due to the differential pricing. (2) Regarding fears of discrepancies in settlement and how to take effective measures: It was resolved to convene an emergency joint meeting of managers and runners from various businesses in the industry to ensure that everyone adheres to the agreed dyeing prices for the current settlement. If any silk shop does not settle according to the agreed dyeing price, it will be deemed as violating laws, contracts, and the promise made when stamping the agreement. Collective sanctions and legal sanctions should be taken: A. (Methods of collective sanctions): If any silk shop does not settle dyeing accounts according to the agreed dyeing price and causes discrepancies, all members of the industry should unanimously refuse to dye goods for that silk shop. B. (Methods of legal sanctions): Regarding silk shops that violate laws and contracts in settling dyeing prices, in addition to collective sanctions, legal action should be taken according to the valid spirit of the laws and contracts, and they should be prosecuted for the crime of breach of trust under Article 363 of the Criminal Code.

Chinese Institute of Engineers Organizes a Sichuan Exploration Group

Twenty-Three Members Divided Into Eleven Groups

Departure for Exploration Set for April 15

Sichuan's treasures are no less abundant than those of the rest of the country, but years of frequent wars and long distances have prevented people from paying close attention. It is now known that the Chinese Institute of Engineers, at the invitation of Liu Xiang, the Reconstruction Director of Sichuan, plans to organize a special Sichuan exploration group to enter Sichuan for exploration. All travel expenses will be borne by the Director's Office. The exploration group has already been organized, with a total of 23 members divided into 11 groups. Qingdao Municipal Government Forms Special Investigation Group to Shanghai

Investigating National Municipal Administration

Focusing on Port Affairs and Railways

Mr. Shen Honglie, the Mayor of Qingdao, in order to organize municipal administration and develop port affairs, has specially formed a municipal investigation group to go to major ports, special municipalities, and port coasts across the country for on-site investigation. As Qingdao Port and Jiaoji Railway have a connected relationship, the Jiaoji Railway also temporarily sent representatives to join. When the members of each group were about to depart, the Longhai Railway received the news and also requested to join members to inspect various places together. The group first went to Hong Kong and Guangdong, then to Shanghai, and has been conducting inspections in Shanghai for several days, extremely busy. Our reporter specially visited the residences of the members yesterday and received detailed information. The details are as follows:

Motivation for Organization

Qingdao's municipal administration has been progressing rapidly in recent years. The number of people from all over the country who come to Qingdao to escape the summer heat and travel is increasing day by day. Since the opening of the Shanghai-Qingdao special liner service by China Merchants Sanbei and other national steamships, port affairs have also become increasingly developed. Even land prices and construction projects have risen. In order to promote the development of joint transportation on various lines, a municipal investigation group was specially organized, and commissioners were assigned to various places in the city to conduct on-site inspections of various port cities across the country as a reference for reform. The types of investigations conducted by the group members are municipal administration, customs, port affairs, and railways.

Number of Members

The investigation group formed by the Qingdao Municipal Government is led by Wang Xichang, Deputy Director of the Port Affairs Bureau of the city, as well as Tai Guisen, Technician of the Port Affairs Bureau, and Gao Zhishu, Technician of the Public Works Bureau. Those joining from the Jiaoji Railway are Yi Shuigui, Deputy Director of the Vehicle Affairs Department, and Meng Xiuwei, Technician of the railway. Qin Yulin, Technician of the Longhai Railway, temporarily requested to join. There are a total of six members. All expenses required by the group are borne by the Qingdao Municipal Government. They departed from Qingdao on January 15th.

First to Hong Kong and Guangdong

This time, the Qingdao Municipal Government's investigation group must visit all major ports and cities across the country. It was decided to first go to South China, then to Central China, and finally to North China. Therefore, on January 15th, they took a steamer from Qingdao to Shanghai. At that time, they were eager to go to Hong Kong, so they transferred to the Empress of Japan steamer on the 17th and arrived in Hong Kong on the 20th. The members of each group explained the purpose of the investigation to the Governor of Hong Kong and requested to visit the various port affairs agencies and railway conditions. They were warmly welcomed by the Governor in Hong Kong. They toured for four days and obtained a lot of reference materials on municipal administration.

Returning to Shanghai from Guangdong

On the 24th of last month, they transferred from Hong Kong to Guangzhou to contact the Guangzhou Municipal Government, and were warmly welcomed by Mayor Liu Jiwen. They stayed in Guangzhou for a total of five days. They thoroughly investigated the new construction, port affairs, railways, warehouses, and wharf facilities in Guangzhou, and consulted the regulations for all content management and other methods. At the end of the month, they returned to Hong Kong and took the Changxing Russian Queen steamer to Shanghai, arriving in Shanghai on the 2nd of this month.

Investigating Shanghai

Shanghai is a special city and a place where Chinese and foreign people gather. The shipping industry is the most developed, ranking first in the country's port affairs, so it is particularly valued by the group. Starting on the 3rd, all the members of the group requested to visit Mayor Wu to observe the municipal administration and investigate the various agencies under the municipal government, conducting classified and detailed investigations for six days. It was only completed yesterday. After the municipal administration examination, they also inspected the Beijing-Shanghai Railway to obtain information for the reform of the Jiaoji Railway.

Departing for Qingdao This Morning

Yesterday, the reporter met with Mr. Xiong, Mr. Qin, and others and asked about the results of the investigation. Mr. Xiong, as a port affairs expert, said that the port affairs conditions in Hong Kong, Guangdong, and Shanghai are different, and each has its own characteristics. There are many resources available to the Qingdao Municipal Government. This trip has yielded a wealth of information, which will be reported and announced after it is sorted out in the future. However, the inspection tour of this group is not yet halfway through. Central China and North China also need to be investigated. Only because it is currently the end of the lunar year, it is inevitable that customs will be followed everywhere. Therefore, we have decided to return to Qingdao first and wait until after this Spring Festival holiday before going to Yantai, Tianjin, and other places. Each member of the group will leave Shanghai for Qingdao on the Dalian Maru steamer at 9:00 this morning.

The Huge Fraud Case of the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China Concluded Yesterday

Sentencing Scheduled for the Morning of the 12th

French Police Continue to Arrest a Legal Person

The criminals arrested in the case of the huge fraud against the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China, six people of Chinese and Russian nationality, have been prosecuted by the police to the First Special District Court. The various situations of the trial have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qian ordered the six defendants to be brought to court again, and the two Japanese who made the copper plate and printed the counterfeit checks were summoned again to prove that the copper plate was indeed manufactured and printed by Sarnick. At this point in the trial, after all the witnesses in the case had been examined, he ordered the debate to begin. First, the police lawyers Ru Baoyi and Li Zhishan rose to argue, elaborating on the crimes of the defendants and analyzing in detail the division of labor and cooperation of the defendants in forging false checks and defrauding huge sums of money, requesting that they be convicted and sentenced according to the charged articles of law. Then, lawyer Fes rose to defend the defendants Jiaosai Fuaier Ahni and his adopted son Ximarasikai, saying that the main person in the case was actually the Englishman Mark, and the first defendant only played a helping role, while the third defendant only obeyed the orders of the first defendant, and should not be held responsible for the crime. Lawyer Mao Xianshen then rose to defend the third defendant Wang Chungan, saying that although Wang took the old checks of the Chartered Bank and handed them over to the first defendant, he did not know their purpose at first. After that, he was divided into stolen foreign goods, even if he had clearly understood, he was only responsible for receiving stolen goods, etc., and defended to the court. The fourth defendant Xie Pingfeng was defended by three lawyers, Zhang Chongding, Fan Gang, and Wang Jian. Fan and Wang based their arguments on the facts of the case, saying that Xie was entrusted by the first defendant to print checks at the Lianyi Printing House and did not know that they were used for defrauding money, and requested that Xie be declared innocent. Lawyer Zhang then expressed his views on legal points, saying that Xie introduced the printing of checks, but he did not know the purpose of the checks, so he was unaware of the fraud. Since he was unaware, it was not intentional, and there was no intention to defraud. As for the money given to Xie by the first defendant afterwards, even if Xie had expected the source of the money at this time, it was only known afterwards and was equivalent to receiving stolen goods. Then, lawyer Lin Yingqing defended the fifth defendant Sarnick, and lawyer Fan rose again to defend the sixth defendant Yang Cailin. The reasons he held were similar to those for defending Xie Pingfeng. Finally, lawyer Li Zhishan slightly refuted the words of the various defenders. Judge Qian then made a final inquiry to the defendants and then announced the end of the debate, scheduling a public sentencing for the morning of the 12th. Except for Ximarasikai, who had been allowed bail, the other five defendants were still taken back to the police station for custody. It is also known that a Portuguese employee of the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China, who participated in defrauding the money, has been arrested by the Portuguese consul in Shanghai. It is now scheduled to be tried in the Portuguese Consulate on the 12th. The Portuguese consul has already sent a letter to the police station yesterday, requesting that all those who should testify in the case be ordered to be present at the time to be questioned.

The Da Mei Evening News reported that Mr. Mark, the Englishman who is the manager of Pu Xi Foreign Company, is one of the defendants in the case of the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China being defrauded of more than 130,000 yuan. This morning (9th), he was tried by the British Consular Police Court. Mr. Sykes, an accountant of the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China, Mr. White, an accountant of the British American Tobacco Company, and a certain Mr. Zhu from the deposit department of the Guohua Bank all testified in court one after another. Mr. White claimed that the money was not paid to any commercial firm, and the signature on the check was not in the handwriting of himself or Mr. Peacock. The defendant Mr. Mark strongly argued that he had nothing to do with the case. This case is expected to not be able to be decided for a while.

The Continental Daily reported that the French Concession Police arrested a legal person born in Russia yesterday (8th), which is related to the case of the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China being defrauded of a huge sum of money. He will be escorted to the French Consular Police Court for trial this morning. It is said that this person once served in the French Commercial Counsellor's Office for three or four months.

The Mail Clerk Was Too Absurd, Concealing More Than a Thousand Letters Without Sending Them

Tearing off the Stamps on the Letters and Converting Them into Cash

American Dollar Notes Worth Seven Yuan Were Also Found on His Person

The Laozha Police Station received a phone report from a Westerner from the Meifeng Bank on Nanjing Road, No. 29, at about 9:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, stating that most of the important letters and documents issued by the bank from July last year to the present have not been received, and there may be other circumstances involved. Please investigate in detail. The chief immediately ordered Western Detective Ding Tuo and Chinese Detective Li Yidong to go to the Meifeng Bank for on-site investigation. After a long time, they discovered that Zhang Shousan, a native of Baoshan and a mail clerk of the company, was suspected of being seriously involved. He was arrested and taken to the police station for a search. Evidence of a kind was found on Zhang's person, namely American dollar bills worth seven yuan, one for five yuan and two for one yuan, which were sealed in a letter by Miss Roman, a Western woman from the Meifeng Bank, on August 9 last year and instructed to be sent to the United States. After the Chinese and Western detectives obtained the clues, they took Zhang to his residence at No. 3, Lane 599, Zhejiang Road, and found more than 1,016 letters from the Meifeng Bank to various countries, as well as two bundles of paper, two sets of calendars, a photo album, and five paper bags, all of which were secretly stolen by Zhang and brought home. Moreover, there was a letter with a check attached, which was taken back to the police station for custody. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Court's Criminal Court No. 1. Lawyer Li Zhishan of the police station rose to describe the course of the case in detail, saying that the circumstances of this case are serious, and the police believe that there is still a need for detailed investigation, so Zhang Shousan has not been formally prosecuted, and requested that he be detained and the date of the trial be changed. When questioned, Zhang Shousan confessed that he went to the Meifeng Bank as a mail clerk in February last year, and his monthly salary was initially only 15 yuan, but it has now increased to 25 yuan. However, two yuan must be deducted for savings every month, which is really not enough to cover expenses. He was forced by economic circumstances to take this measure. He also admitted that he did have more than a thousand letters that he withheld and did not send, and tore off the stamps to convert them into cash, totaling more than 200 yuan before and after. This matter started in July last year and lasted until October, only three months. As for the American dollar bills worth seven yuan that were taken from his person, because Miss Roman did not seal the mouth of the letter tightly and the corner of the bill was exposed on the outside, he thought it was a fun thing, so he took it down, etc. After Feng Shide, the presiding judge, verified the confession, he instructed that Zhang be allowed to be detained and wait for the trial to be changed to the 21st.

Deng Darong Convicted

Sentenced to Six Years in Prison

Deng Darong, a native of Guangdong and a staff member of the Audit Section of the First Division of the Su, Zhe, and Anhui District Unified Tax Bureau, was found to have forged the seal of Director Wang Shoushu, fraudulently obtained checkbooks, and fraudulently withdrawn tax funds of 84,321.21 yuan from the Central Bank in succession. The director of the bureau discovered this, sent it to the Public Security Bureau, and transferred it to the detention center of the First Special District Court for temporary detention. He also hired a lawyer to file a complaint. The Special Court has concluded the trial and is waiting for the sentencing. This has been reported in this newspaper for several times. Yesterday afternoon, Trial Judge Liu Yugui came to Criminal Court No. 8 to announce the verdict. The main text of the judgment is: Deng Darong's continuous use of forged negotiable securities is sentenced to six years in prison. The number of days detained before the judgment is final shall be offset against the prison term at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The forged seal and two check stubs from the Central Bank are confiscated. The defendant shall compensate the plaintiff 84,321.21 yuan. He will be temporarily detained in the detention center during the appeal period.

Extorting 2,500 Gold Coins Sent to the Second Special District Citizens' Association

Zhou Chunxiu and Li Jiatai Arrested at the Same Time

Fan Rencai Became Enemies with Others Due to Official Duties

There was a huge swindler named Liang Kexi who falsely established the Hexing Trading Company on Yuanmingyuan Road last winter and opened current accounts with various foreign banks in this name. Before long, all the banks he had dealings with were overdrawn, totaling about 160,000 gold coins. The Meifeng Bank on Nanjing Road was also one of the defrauded parties. However, Fan Rencai, an employee of the bank, discovered it early, so only 5,000 gold coins were overdrawn at that time. Fan immediately demanded the money from Liang, and Liang was also afraid that the incident would become uncontrollable, so he repaid the debt owed to Meifeng and then fled with the money. When other banks reported to the police, Liang had already disappeared without a trace, and his whereabouts have not been detected until now. Therefore, this fraud case is currently at a standstill. Since Fan discovered that Liang was a swindler and recovered the debt, Meifeng suffered no loss. It was indeed fortunate. However, Fan had made enemies with others. At the end of last month, Fan suddenly received a threatening letter accusing Fan of colluding with Liang to carry out the fraud and demanding that Fan quickly hand over half of the 5,000 gold coins he had obtained from Liang, otherwise the fraud and inside stories would be exposed in the newspapers. He was asked to post a notice in the newspaper immediately. Fan told the bank's manager and reported it to the General Police Station for investigation. He also posted an advertisement in the Times on February 2, 3, and 4 as instructed in the letter, signed (Tian Tian). On the 7th, Fan received a phone call saying that they had sent a second letter and could handle it according to the instructions in the letter. At this time, Fan had not yet received the so-called second letter. He still reported to the General Police Station and sent Detective Gao Zhen to the post office with the Mail Inspection Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau to check the letters. Soon, the letter was found, and after opening it, it instructed Fan to place the money in a shoebox at 4:00 p.m. on the 8th and send it to the second floor of the Second Special District Citizens' Association at No. 112, Yideli Road, Weier Meng Road in the French Concession. He only needed to leave the box and not say much. Detective Gao then made a package according to the instructions, filled the box with waste paper instead of banknotes, carried it to the place, and saw Zhou Chunxiu and Li Jiatai, two cadres of the association, sitting in the meeting. When Zhou saw Detective Gao, a look of panic suddenly appeared on his face, and he wanted to get up and receive the box. Gao immediately questioned him, and Zhou became impatient and reluctantly took the box and threw it on the table, and deliberately said to Li that he did not know who sent the box. Detective Gao felt that these two people were very suspicious, so he re-entered the room with the detectives sent by the French police, and saw that the rope on the box had been untied, the lid of the box had been opened, and the paper stacked in the box was also messy. He arrested the two people and took the box back to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court and tried by Judge Feng Shide. First, lawyer Li Zhishan of the police station described the course of the case, saying that the case still needs to be investigated and requested a change of date. Zhou and Li also hired lawyers such as Jie Gang to defend them. Judge Feng approved the detention and changed the date for another trial.

Collision of Rice Boats and Sugar Boats

The Bow Was Broken and the Escort Drowned

Who Will Compensate for the Losses of Each Party?

Qin Decheng, a rice boat from Jiangsu, was recently hired by the Shanghai rice merchant Heji Company to load 190 shi of white rice to transport to Shanghai. Because the end of the lunar year was approaching, he was eager to transport the rice to Shanghai. He instructed Qin's boat to set sail so that it could arrive in Shanghai as soon as possible. A apprentice, Jin Jinsheng, was also sent to escort the boat. The boat set sail for Shanghai after loading the goods the day before yesterday. When it reached the north entrance of the Mahe River in Southern Huangpu, it happened to have a tailwind, so it hoisted its sails and sailed very fast. Shen Chunlin's boat, loaded with seafood, sugar, and northern goods from a certain company in Jiaxing, was sailing south. The two boats were sailing close to each other head-on at that place. They were each turning their rudders to avoid each other, but Qin's boat was faster due to the tailwind. It was too late to avoid each other, and the two boats collided violently. The bow of Qin's boat was broken, and the escort, Jin Jinsheng, was knocked into the water. Although Shen's boat was larger, it was very old, and the bow was broken off. Water immediately poured in, and it gradually sank. Both boats called for help. Fortunately, a Huzhou steamer happened to pass by and saw them and went forward to rescue Jin Jinsheng, who had fallen into the water. He was not found. The sinking boat was rescued first and taken to the beach to be stranded. Then, Qin's boat was towed to a shallow beach and stopped. However, after the collision, both boats had cracks in their hulls, and the goods inside were wet. Qin reported to the cargo owner yesterday because Jin Jinsheng was missing, requesting negotiations. Both sides had their own reasons and refused to be held responsible for compensation. However, rice and sugar are both items that cannot be soaked in water, and now they have been damaged, resulting in a great loss. The Heji hired a boat to transfer the rice from Qin's boat to Shanghai and entrusted someone to pay attention to finding the body.

Chen Lifu Talks About Chinese Movies

At Present, We Need to Focus on Nationalism

We Must Recognize the Content of Production and Education Films

A Reporter from the Nanjing Central News Agency Visited Central Committee Member Chen Lifu for Business, and He Mentioned the Issue of Chinese Movies in the Middle of the Conversation. His Words Were Profound and Hit the Current Malpractice. They Are Recorded as Follows. Mr. Chen Said, "The Chinese Film Industry Has Made Extremely Rapid Progress Compared to Previous Years, and the Audience Welcomes Domestically Produced Films Extremely Warmly. This is Really a Good Phenomenon for the Future of the Domestically Produced Film Industry. However, Some Businessmen Engaged in the Film Industry Still Cannot Recognize the Path That Domestically Produced Films Should Take, and Neglect the Requirements of the Times and National Character, and the Significance of Film Education, Which Affects the Credit and Authority of the Domestically Produced Film Industry to No Small Extent. This is Really a Pity. It is Even More Heartbreaking to Pick Up My Previous Words and Conversations About the Issue of Movies, Forcefully and Arbitrarily Interpret Them, and Use Them as a Cover for Proletarian-Consciousness Movies. You Must Know That Proletarian-Consciousness Films Can Never Be Used to Confuse the Issues of National Independence and People's Livelihood Development. Movies That Promote the National Spirit Must Stand on the Position of Fighting for the Survival of the Entire Nation and Create an Immortal Cause. They Are Definitely Not Proletarian Works Aimed at Inciting the Differentiation of All Classes Within the Entire Nation, and They Cannot Be Falsely Borrowed to Replace Them. (Force) is the Main Element to Promote National Unity and All Construction Progress, and It Is Also the Main Expression of National Unity, But It Can Never Be Achieved by the Way of Riots That Harm the Country and the Nation. The Movie Art That the Current National Revolution Urgently Needs Is Based on Nationalism, Aiming at Promoting the Culture and Spirit of the Entire Nation as Its Main Purpose and Task. It Can Never Be Confused and Arbitrarily Interpreted by Proletarian Films That Incite Class Opposition, Provoke the Struggle Between the Rich and the Poor, Betray the Interests of the National State, and Perform Riots in a Riotous Way. As for Production and Education Films, We Must Especially Recognize the Content of Production and Education. We Must Never Mix Fish Eyes with Pearls and Falsely Associate Proletarian-Consciousness Works with Production and Education Films. I Sincerely Hope That My Colleagues in the Chinese Film Industry Will Pay Attention to This Point."

Jianghai Customs Notice Regarding Regulations for the Transfer of Imported Raw Materials

Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of the Jiangwan Customs, and Bretschneider, Commissioner of Customs, issued Notice No. 1339 yesterday to regulate the transfer of goods manufactured using imported foreign raw materials to domestic ports. The notice states: "Goods manufactured in China using parts imported from abroad, marked with the country of origin, when transported from one treaty port to another, must be declared by the reporting merchant in the manifest, specifying whether the goods are entirely or partially made from imported foreign goods with markings. Supporting documentation must be submitted to Customs for inspection, so that the imported packaging of the constituent parts can also be examined. All merchants must comply accordingly. This notice is hereby issued."

Dispute Over Small Sanbei Vessel Resolved Through Negotiations Between Both Parties Yesterday

Twenty-Eight Original Workers Retained

Date of Embarkation to Be Determined by the Company

The Dagoong Sheh reports that the small Sanbei vessel, operated by the Sanbei Company on the Shanghai-Zhenjiang line, was reassigned to the Yangtze River route on the 21st of last month, resulting in the dismissal of all 31 mess hall workers on the vessel. This aroused the dissatisfaction of all the workers, who requested assistance from the Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee. The committee sent Secretary Sun Lyping to negotiate with the Sanbei Company. As General Manager Yu Qiaqing was in Beijing at the time, a temporary solution was agreed upon with the company: 15 of the dismissed workers would be reinstated to work on the vessel first, and the rest would wait for Yu Qiaqing to come to Shanghai for further negotiations. Yesterday, the committee again sent Secretaries Hou Dachun and Sun Lyping to the company for negotiations, and they were received by General Manager Yu Qiaqing. As a result of the negotiations, it was decided to retain 28 of the original second-class workers to work on the vessel. However, the date of resumption of work must be formally notified by the company before they can board the vessel. Both parties expressed satisfaction and declared the matter resolved.

Workers on Wusong Steamer to Resume Work Today After Resolution of Dispute

Seamen's Union to Send Representatives to Accompany Workers on Board

The Dagoong Sheh reports that the case of the British Taikoo Company expelling second-class workers on the Wusong steamer has been resolved after the Chinese Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee sent representatives to negotiate with the company authorities repeatedly. On the 31st of last month, an agreement with seven points of resolution was signed with the company. Of the 126 dismissed workers, 86 will receive a subsidy of 30 yuan each from the company and wait for other Taikoo vessels to need them before returning to work. The remaining 40 will still go to work on the Wusong steamer. The vessel returned to Shanghai from Wuhan yesterday and is scheduled to sail out tonight. All 40 workers will gather at the Seamen's Union in Ximen at 3:00 PM today. The committee will send Secretaries Hou Dachun and Sun Lyping to escort them to resume work on the Wusong steamer at the Bund outside Xinkaihe. Photographs will be taken at that time to commemorate the event.

Municipal Bureau of Public Works to Construct Pier No. 11

Zhongfa Qiuxin Factory Wins the Bid to Construct

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works is constructing Pier No. 11, a public wharf for steamships, at Maojia Lane in South Shanghai to meet the needs of steamship companies and berthing vessels. The all-steel floating pier is 18 zhang (approx. 60 meters) long and 2.4 zhang (approx. 8 meters) wide, with two floating bridges, each 1.6 zhang (approx. 5.3 meters) wide and 3.5 zhang (approx. 11.7 meters) long. The design is well-conceived. Bids were opened on the afternoon of February 7. Six companies submitted bids, including Hexing Factory, Da Zhonghua, Hengchangxiang, Caili, Yuanda, and Zhongfa Qiuxin Factory. After review, Zhongfa Qiuxin Factory won the bid with a price of 34,900 yuan. The Bureau of Public Works has prepared a contract and sent a letter to Qiuxin Factory to sign the contract as soon as possible so that construction can begin and be completed and put into use in three months.

22nd Year of Work

The North-China Daily News reports that the Rickshaw Men's Gospel Mission released its 22nd annual report yesterday (8th). The report states that in the year ending October 31, 1933, the mission received a total of 12,827.09 yuan in public donations, including 9,733.81 yuan collected by the North-China Daily News on behalf of Christmas donations and 1,800 yuan donated by the Shanghai Race Club. The balance sheet shows total assets of 134,958.93 yuan. The income for the year exceeded expenditures by 702.33 yuan. The Use of Dictionaries

A learned person is not necessarily someone who can (remember) many technical terms and specialized vocabulary and (understand) their meanings. Primarily, it is someone who can (find) their origins and their meanings. This is because reading is not just about memorization; understanding is key. Moreover, simply memorizing numerous terms and jargon, no matter how much or how broadly one remembers them, is actually of little use. Any rudimentary dictionary is far superior. Human memory is ultimately limited. However, encountering these terms while reading and not understanding them is not only regrettable but also greatly hinders comprehension. Therefore, (memorizing) the meanings of terms is not entirely necessary (though knowing important terms and their meanings is necessary), but (being able to look them up) is essential.

The only way to understand (technical terms) is to consult dictionaries. In recent years, China's cultural endeavors, while still far behind Western standards, have indeed made considerable progress compared to previous years. Considering only dictionaries, many types have been published in recent years. Although few are meticulously edited, having a bad dictionary is better than having none. Finding nothing in dictionaries, as mentioned in your letter, does not mean (using dictionaries) is wrong. Besides consulting dictionaries, what better method is there? While you may lack teachers and friends, even with many knowledgeable friends, you know that (one or two teachers and friends) cannot completely answer everything. But why does your difficulty arise? Most likely, the dictionary you are using is not comprehensive enough. For example, the "Ciyuan" dictionary covers a wide range of categories, but its volumes are limited. How could it possibly include all past and present terms? It can only include the important ones, and it emphasizes (classical) terms, with fewer modern terms included. However, the purpose of a dictionary is to allow us to find whatever we want at any time. Therefore, our standard for choosing a dictionary is not how many categories it includes but whether it comprehensively covers the terms within the categories it does include. The number of categories is a secondary issue. Therefore, you should purchase dictionaries for the subjects you are studying, and avoid buying too many general dictionaries.

If you enjoy reading novels and literature, there are dictionaries for this area such as "Literary Dictionary," "New Literature Dictionary," and "New Literature Description Dictionary," etc. For studying economics, there is the "Economics Dictionary" (edited by Ke Xiangnian). However, based on your letter, it seems that you are not struggling with terms when researching a specific subject but rather encountering many terms that you don't understand while reading casually. Therefore, you still seem to need a dictionary that covers a wide range of categories and includes commonly used words. In this case, the "Modern Language Dictionary" (edited by Li Dingsheng) and the "New Terminology Dictionary" (edited by Ke Bonian, et al.) would be quite helpful. These two books are quite comprehensive and the writing is clear. However, many explanations lack precision, so they should only be used for reference. It is absolutely not advisable to treat their explanations as definitions.

If you encounter terms that you cannot find explanations for anywhere, you can send a letter to this newspaper, and we will do our best to find their origins and explanations for you. – Yi Kang
