Ministry of Education Actively Provides Relief for Education of Youths from the Northeast

Establishing an Office in Beiping

The Ministry of Education's measures for providing relief to unemployed youths from the Northeast were briefly reported in yesterday's newspaper. It has been learned that after the Executive Yuan approved the principles, the (Provisional Relief Measures for Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast) were drafted immediately. Yesterday, instructions were issued to the relevant offices to comply. At the same time, because the majority of youths from the Northeast are scattered in the north, the relief efforts will begin with investigations in the north. Therefore, Nanjing will only have the name of the Relief Office, while the actual relief work will be carried out by establishing an office in Beiping to oversee everything locally. Director Zhou Tianfang has already gone to Beiping to organize the office. Yesterday, the Ministry of Education approved the (Regulations for the Beiping Office of the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast) and the (Provisional Relief Measures for Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast), which are recorded separately as follows:

Regulations for the Beiping Office of the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast

Article 1: The Beiping Office of the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast is established in accordance with Article 2 of the Organization Regulations to carry out the task of investigating and providing relief to diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast in various provinces and cities in North China under the command of the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast.

Article 2: The staff of this office shall be transferred from the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast.

Article 3: The work status and financial situation of this office shall be submitted monthly by the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast for compilation and reporting.

Article 4: The expenses required for investigative matters of this office shall be drawn from the contingency fund of the relief funds, with actual expenses reported and reimbursed. However, if the monthly expenditure exceeds 300 yuan, the office shall first submit a request to the Ministry of Education for approval.

Article 5: The seal of this office shall be issued by the Ministry of Education upon request from the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast.

Article 6: Detailed rules for the operation of this office shall be determined separately.

Article 7: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of approval and may be amended upon request if there are any omissions.

Provisional Relief Measures for Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast

The Ministry of Education has established provisional relief measures for diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast, which have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing. The details of these measures are as follows:

1. (To expand education and cultivate national strength, diligent and ambitious students from the Northeast (referring to the provinces and cities of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and Harbin) who have been forced or voluntarily entered through the passes to pursue education shall be provided with relief in accordance with these measures.

2. The affairs of providing relief to diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast shall be handled by the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast established by the Ministry of Education.

3. The relief measures are temporarily divided into the following four types:

(1) The Ministry of Education shall continue to issue orders to all public and private schools at all levels nationwide to exempt diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast who have been verified by the school as genuine from tuition fees.

(2) Provide subsidies to those who are genuinely unable to afford the costs of food, lodging, and books but have excellent academic performance.

(3) Establish schools specifically for training students from the Northeast.

(4) Establish quotas for students from the Northeast studying abroad.

4. The subsidies mentioned in item (2) above shall be granted only to those who meet the qualifications specified in the same item. The Relief Office shall establish a review committee to handle the matter and submit it to the Ministry of Education for approval. The review standards and procedures shall be determined separately.

5. The number of subsidized students and the amount of subsidies for each level of school shall be separately drafted by the Relief Office based on the actual situation and needs and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

6. The granting of subsidies may be decided by the Relief Office through examinations when necessary. The subsidy period for subsidized students who have passed the review or examination shall be one academic year, and shall be re-evaluated upon expiration.

7. In order to concentrate the training of students from the Northeast and meet their needs, secondary schools specifically for students from the Northeast shall be established in appropriate locations, including junior high schools, senior high schools, junior vocational schools, senior vocational schools, and equivalent supplementary classes. Supplementary education shall be provided to students who have graduated from schools outside the passes to supplement their knowledge of civics, history, and geography and to provide training. After passing the examination, their academic qualifications shall be confirmed to facilitate further education.

8. In order to cultivate ambitious youths from the Northeast into specialized talents, quotas for students from the Northeast studying abroad shall be established. The Relief Office shall submit a request to the Ministry of Education to hold examinations to select candidates. These quotas may temporarily be filled by selecting those public and self-funded students who went abroad before September 18th who are unable to maintain their studies and have excellent grades. The monthly expenses for each student from the Northeast studying abroad shall be determined by the Relief Office with reference to the tuition fees of general government-funded students studying abroad and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval.

9. Northeast students who have received relief under the above articles shall have their relief qualifications revoked if they have any of the following circumstances. If the circumstances are more serious, the benefits they have already received shall be recovered. Separate management rules shall be established:

(1) Violating school rules and being expelled from school or having received two major demerits.

(2) Repeating a grade twice during the course of study.

(3) Not complying with the rules and orders of the Relief Office.

(4) Engaging in conduct that does not respect national honor and interests.

10. The organization of the Relief Office for Education of Youths from the Northeast shall be determined by the Ministry of Education through a ministerial order.

11. The funds specifically for providing relief to diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast are temporarily set at 27,500 yuan per month, which shall be paid by the national treasury.

12. These measures shall be submitted by the Ministry of Education to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation.

Jiangsu Education Department Designates Personnel to Depart for Japan on March 1st for Observation

Key Points for Observing Secondary Schools, Normal Schools, Vocational Schools, and Social Education Determined

Responsibilities for Communication, Documentation, General Affairs, and Accounting Also Assigned

(Zhenjiang News) In order to improve education in Jiangsu Province, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education previously selected nine individuals from across the province to observe the state of education in Japan. These were: Cao Chu, the principal of Zhenjiang Normal School; Huang Tongyi, the principal of Qixia Rural Normal School; Teng Songshi, the principal of Huangdu Rural Normal School; Zhou Houchu, the principal of Yangzhou School; Yan Liyang, the principal of Xu Middle School; Deng Bangti, the principal of Suzhou Industrial School; Shen Shanzhi, the principal of Zhenjiang Normal School Affiliated Primary School; Sheng Langxi, the principal of Shanghai Experimental Primary School; and Zhao Hongqian, the director of the Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Public Education Center. This was previously reported in this newspaper. At 11:00 AM on the 8th, Director Zhou of the Education Department convened a meeting at the department to discuss the key points of the observation and decided that the departure would be before March 1st. The details are as follows:

[Director Zhou's Remarks

At 11:00 AM on the 8th, Director Zhou convened the team of observers at the department. The department heads were also in attendance. Director Zhou stated briefly that, in addition to the prescribed observation points, the following points should be given special attention:

(1) Regarding secondary education, attention should be paid to: 1. Student training issues, including how teachers and staff cooperate with the principal to train youth, and how government officials supervise teachers and staff to take responsibility for training youth. 2. Issues regarding the future prospects of secondary school students.

(2) Regarding primary education, attention should be paid to: 1. How labor education is implemented. 2. How health education is conducted. 3. How local teaching materials are compiled.

(3) Regarding social education, attention should be paid to: 1. Methods for promoting people's side occupations. 2. Methods for training the people, such as the organization of youth groups.

The meeting concluded at 12:00 PM. The key points for each observation are summarized as follows:

Key Points for Observation

Secondary Education: (1) School administration. (2) Teaching situation. (3) Student training situation. (4) Equipment status. (5) Guidance on further education and employment.

Normal School: (1) School administration. (2) Teaching situation. (A) Normal school. (B) Rural normal school. (C) Differences between normal schools and rural normal schools. (3) Student training situation. (A) Normal school. (B) Rural normal school. (C) Differences between normal schools and rural normal schools. (4) Equipment status. (5) Internship methods. (6) The relationship between normal schools and the environment. (A) The relationship between normal schools and urban environments. (B) The relationship between rural normal schools and rural environments. (7) Plans for normal schools to improve local education. (A) How normal schools improve local education. (B) How rural normal schools improve rural education. (8) Employment status of graduates. (9) Special facilities.

Vocational School: (1) School administration. (2) Teaching situation. (3) Student training situation. (4) Equipment status. (5) Internship methods. (6) Production situation. (7) Connection with local industries. (8) Improving local industries. (9) Employment prospects of graduates. (10) Special facilities.

Primary Education: 1. Health education. 2. Labor education and production education. 3. Civic education. 4. Science education. 5. Local education. 6. Normal school student internships. 7. Teacher training. 8. Sources and distribution of primary school funding.

Social Education: Key points for observing social education in Japan:

(1) Japanese social education administration. A. Central social education administration. B. Local social education administration. C. Social education administration system.

(2) Japanese social education funding. A. Sources of social education funding. B. Statistics on central and local social education funding. C. Distribution of social education funding.

(3) The background of Japanese social education. A. Socio-economic situation. B. People's living conditions. C. People's educational level.

(4) Social education for youth training. A. Youth training organizations and their organizational structure. B. Types and implementation of youth training programs. C. Actual guidance from the central and local governments for youth.

(5) Social education programs for adult learning. A. Adult learning programs organized by the government. B. Adult learning programs organized by schools. C. Special facilities of labor schools.

(6) General social education programs. A. Facilities for libraries, museums, and other exhibition programs. B. Facilities for film education and other entertainment programs. C. Implementation of practical supplementary education.

(7) Other. A. Social education programs attached to charitable organizations or business enterprises. B. Other programs with social education characteristics. C. The relationship between general education and social education.

Departure Date

All nine members, except for Deng Bangti, the principal of Suzhou Industrial School, are scheduled to gather in Shanghai on March 1st and then travel east to Japan, first to Tokyo, and then determine their itinerary. They will spend approximately two months observing in Japan. Upon returning home, they plan to detour through northern China for observation.

After the entire group spoke with Director Zhou at the Department of Education, they reconvened in the afternoon. Sheng Langxi has been requested to handle the purchase of boat tickets in Shanghai due to his proximity.

Jiangsu Education Department Order, Starting in the 23rd Year

Ordinary Middle Schools Must Not Expand

Vocational Schools Should Be Expanded

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an order to the education bureaus of various counties stating: "It has been repeatedly ordered by the Ministry of Education since the 20th year to restrict the establishment of ordinary middle schools and actively increase the establishment of vocational schools. Although this department has repeatedly ordered county-run middle schools in various counties to adhere to the single-track system in principle and not arbitrarily expand classes, and has persuaded privately established middle schools to convert to vocational schools, vocational education has still not been fully promoted. Last year, the Ministry of Education issued the 'Standards for the Establishment and Allocation of Funds for Secondary Schools in Various Provinces and Cities,' stipulating that (1) the allocation of secondary education funds in each province and city for vocational schools must not be less than 35 percent (including vocational supplementary schools), normal schools must account for approximately 25 percent, and middle schools must account for approximately 40 percent, limited to achieving the above standards from the 23rd year to the 26th year; (2) the newly added funds for secondary education in each province and city should be used primarily for vocational and normal school funds. Those unable to increase funds should gradually reduce the corresponding amount of middle school funds from the existing funds to expand vocational education and normal school education; (3) the above standards and deadlines are equally applicable to county-run middle schools throughout the province, and each department should plan, supervise, and handle them throughout the province; (4) each department should supervise and urge privately established middle schools to convert to vocational schools or vocational supplementary schools in order to achieve a state of balanced development between private middle schools and private vocational schools by the 26th year of the Republic of China, which is currently under review. The provincial government ordered (starting from the 23rd year, ordinary middle school classes in this province should be restricted and not arbitrarily expanded for enrollment, and strict admission should be enforced, with the total number not exceeding the number of the previous year), which should be followed and circulated for compliance. According to this order, the allocation of funds for secondary schools in various counties shows that ordinary middle schools account for the most, and vocational schools are often non-existent. As a result, ordinary middle schools are expanding daily, and vocational schools are rarely developing. Such a distorted state is difficult to improve the efficiency of secondary education as a whole. The 23rd year is approaching in an instant. The measures for secondary schools in various counties, except for normal schools, which will be separately ordered, are now stipulated as follows: (1) County-run middle schools that originally operated on a single track must not expand classes on the pretext of a large number of students going on to higher education. Those that originally operated on a double track should gradually reduce enrollment starting from the 23rd year and convert to a single track by the 26th year. The admission of students should be strictly enforced. (2) Counties that have already established vocational schools should find ways to expand them. Those that have not established them should immediately plan to establish them. The funds should be offset by the reduced middle school funds or newly added funds. If funds are limited, vocational supplementary schools should also be planned to train students who cannot go on to higher education with practical skills. (3) Privately established middle schools that have been registered should be supervised and urged to reduce ordinary classes and gradually convert to vocational schools in areas where the establishment of ordinary middle schools is more dense. (4) Starting from the 23rd year, privately established middle schools should be immediately supervised and urged to convert to vocational schools or vocational supplementary schools. If the funds are not very generous, they should be persuaded to convert to primary schools to show restriction. The above clauses regarding county-run secondary schools should be drafted in detail by the principal of the school, and the funds should be included in the 23rd year education budget of the county and reported for approval. Regarding privately established middle schools, they should be supervised and complied with and reported. In addition to separate circulation, this order is hereby issued to the director of the bureau for compliance and circulation to all public and private middle schools under their jurisdiction for compliance, which is hereby ordered."

Jiangsu Education Department Orders Strict Examination of the Conduct of Third-Year Middle School Students

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an order to the education bureaus of various counties, stating: "Middle school students are the backbone of society, and normal school students are the teachers of primary schools. They should strive diligently in their studies and cultivate their character to fulfill this mission. However, the higher the grade level of these students, the less emphasis they place on their studies, the less they abide by order, and the less attention they pay to their conduct. The Director of this Department has observed, as well as according to the reports of various supervisors, that third-year students in various schools often arbitrarily skip classes, their assignments are becoming increasingly lax, they are absent from memorial weeks without reason, they often do not attend morning exercises, and they arbitrarily disrupt order in self-study rooms, dormitories, and dining halls. This is just to mention the most obvious cases, which has led other grades to follow suit, and the academic atmosphere is becoming increasingly arrogant. If the above situations or other violations of school rules occur in the future, the principals of the schools should be held responsible and strictly dealt with, and should not be tolerated. The students should also learn from their mistakes and not neglect the regulations just because graduation is near, thus undoing all their previous efforts. The principals of each school should strictly examine the students' usual conduct and report it at any time. This year's graduation examination for middle school students and the graduation procedures for normal and vocational schools will be determined by this Department with reference to each student's usual conduct, in order to reverse the declining trend. In addition to separate circulation, this order is hereby issued to the director of the bureau for circulation to all public and private middle schools under their jurisdiction for general knowledge and announcement, which is hereby ordered."

Books Approved for Publication Must Not Be Marked with Words Such as "Approved by the Ministry of Education"

Nanjing, 9th - Electric News - At the request of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau, the Ministry of Education recently ordered various departments and bureaus to instruct bookstores under their jurisdiction that all books approved for publication in the future may only indicate on the cover that they have been reviewed and approved for publication by the Ministry of Education as a textbook for a certain purpose, or with the words "Reviewed and Approved for Publication by the Ministry of Education." The use of words such as "Approved by the Ministry of Education" is prohibited. Books approved for publication after revision are also limited to submitting the revised version for review within six months.

Summary of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Education Budget

The Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council has drafted the education budget for 1934 and submitted it to the Board of Directors on Wednesday of this week. After approval by the Board of Directors, it was sent to the Finance Committee for review and compilation. As usual, the temporary expenses are divided into categories A, B, and C. Category A refers to projects that the Board of Directors has already approved or deems urgent. Category B refers to projects that are considered necessary and will be carried out as soon as funds are available. Category C refers to projects that will not be paid for this year due to financial and other reasons.

The temporary expenses for Chinese schools include 25,000 yuan for the installation of heating pipes and boiler rooms at Nie Zhongcheng Public School, marked as Category A; 2,000 yuan for increasing the height of the wall at Chinese Public School, marked as Category A; 280,000 yuan for the new building of Girls' Middle School (already under construction), marked as Category A; and the cost of using the Council's military shed to build a playground at Huishan Road Primary School, also marked as Category A, with the exact amount to be supplemented by the Finance Department. In addition, 11,600 yuan is needed to convert two classrooms and make other modifications to the Kenningham Road Primary School. The Public Works Department believes that this temporary addition is uneconomical and is marked as Category C. Regarding this issue, the Education Committee plans to set a limit on the number of students admitted to each primary school in the future. 10,000 yuan is needed for the addition of a playground and handicraft room at Xinzha Road Primary School. This is considered deferrable, or the military shed could be converted in the future, so it is marked as Category C. 17,000 yuan is needed for the reconstruction of a larger playground at Chinese Public School. It is generally agreed that this can be deferred for one year and is marked as Category C. The temporary expenses for Western schools include 15,000 yuan for the final payment for the construction of Yu Garden Road Western Public School, marked as Category A; 400,000 yuan for the construction of the Hamilton House Western Girls' Public School, marked as Category A; 25,000 yuan for adding and modifying the cooking center at Yu Garden Road Western Girls' Public School, and 6,000 yuan for the playground. Since the old ones have been demolished, there is a need to rebuild them, so they are marked as Category B. As for the regular expenses, after slightly revising and adding comments on the expenses for the Education Department and the six Western schools, they were submitted to the Finance Committee for review.

New Plan for Minzhi Primary and Secondary School

Minzhi Primary and Secondary School Kindergarten has spared no effort in improving all facilities over the years. The number of students has increased year by year, gaining deep social trust. Now, a new policy for children's years has been set: (1) The school is like a family, and teachers and staff care for students as if they were their own children; (2) Education is productive, eliminating all empty theories and impractical things, to benefit students' future and supplement society; (3) Equipment is scientific, further complementing educational and moral education to gradually change and eliminate all bad habits. The topics and styles of Chinese and English essays for the 20th week of this term have been prescribed, divided into stages, and the questions are unified and tested, in order to promote mutual learning. Professors of each subject and extracurricular cultivation are closely linked with the library, science museum, natural history museum, animal garden, aquarium, auditorium, playground, film, broadcasting, etc., and are fully utilized. The school infirmary has added a large amount of medical equipment, and the school doctor examines the physical condition of the students in turn every day to improve children's health. The 14th issue of the school publication has now been published, with content prepared for each subject. Other aspects are still being designed in many ways.

Shanghai-Tianjin-Hong Kong Interport Football General Review

Gathering from the 14th for a Round-Robin Tournament

Tianjin Team's Strength is Stronger, Expected to Win Championship

First Game: Shanghai vs. Tianjin at Shen Garden

The Shanghai-Hong Kong-Tianjin interport football match, Shanghai vs. Hong Kong, or Shanghai vs. Tianjin, is held at least once a year. However, the three teams meeting in Shanghai for a triangular competition has been as far back as 1928, which is already six years ago. This year, they will meet again. The three teams will gather again in Shanghai during the Lunar New Year to compete for the championship trophy. Analysis of Triangular Strength

Shanghai: The strength of the Shanghai interport team has unexpectedly changed greatly in the recent week. The Donghua Association was dissatisfied with the Western United Association's arrangements. Five players selected, including Dai Linjing and Zhou Xianyan, refused to play in the two interport trial matches, resulting in all of them being dropped. Only three Chinese players, including Sun Jinshun, were selected. The strength of the Shanghai team was greatly affected. The current forced lineup, apart from the satisfactory midfield and the relatively reliable defense, is questionable whether goalkeeper Fulushou can play after his injury. Even if he does play, he is only a second-rate player. There are not many talented forwards for shooting. It is very difficult for Shanghai to use Hua Te on the left wing. Compared with Tianjin and Hong Kong, it seems to be inferior.

Hong Kong: Hong Kong is also divided into two teams to deal with Shanghai and Tianjin. The lineup against Tianjin seems to be less strong than the one against Shanghai. The midfield, defense, and forwards are all good, but the goalkeeper is not very good. It is said that Mai Hadi is only a third-rate player. If Bao Jiaping can come, there will be no worries. It is hoped that there will be more strength. The appearance of Da and Xiao Gaoshan Nu in the interport game is the eighth time. In the future, their cooperation with Tan Jiangbai or Zheng Jiliang will be very promising.

Tianjin: Among the three teams, Tianjin is the strongest. The five forwards are all fierce and terrifying. Luo Jie, Jie Hansun, Fenjie, and Swiss are all world-renowned veterans. Qiong Si is also said to be exceptionally good. A Que'er has changed from center forward to left wing. The strength of the midfield is similar to that of Shanghai. Hei Er's header is unique. It is a pity that Da Sifo is not coming due to injury, and goalkeeper Mishakafu has been transferred to defense. The current goalkeeper has good skills. It is still hoped that Tianjin will be stronger.

Although the ball did not go in, the opponent fouled, and they were penalized twice. Tan's free throws are usually known as his forte, but unexpectedly, the first throw missed, and the second throw bounced out. Center Xu Peiran scored 25 points alone, which was a great contribution.

Tongji and Feixia were evenly matched and could be called brothers in distress. The competition between the two teams was very even, but the performance was not very exciting. Zhanghua vs. Chizhi: Although the score was very close in the first half, Chizhi was definitely not an opponent. Although they struggled hard, Zhanghua was still relaxed and content. The first ten minutes of the second half were still uneventful. Afterwards, Zhanghua's work became slightly tighter, and they won 62 to 39.

Smith Will Perform Billiards Skills at Xiqing

Two Games Scheduled for the Evening of the 15th

Li Gongying to Accompany Again

World professional billiard master Willie Smith came to Shanghai for sightseeing this time, and took the opportunity to continue to hold eight performances in four days at the Lianhua General Association. Yesterday, it was over. Man Luojun, the chairman of the billiard committee of the Xiqing Association, specially invited him to perform at the association, and also invited the Chinese Billiard King Li Gongying to participate in order to promote art and promote it. The dates are two games on the afternoon of the 15th at 6:00 PM and 9:15 PM in the evening. The association will start selling admission tickets today. The number of blue seats is limited, and it is feared that they will be turned away at the last minute.

Not in Vain

Smith is known as an all-rounder on the world professional billiards stage. This is his first time in Shanghai. More than a hundred people who admired him went to appreciate his art day and night. Mayor Wu, Secretary-General Yu, Director Pan, Lin Kanghou, Ma Yinliang, etc. of this city have also been guests of honor one after another. After watching, they all praised and deeply felt that this kind of skill is indeed rare in the country, and there is a need to promote it. The general Chinese and Western billiards players are even more concerned, paying attention to the way he holds the cue and the way he uses it in order to understand the principle. Therefore, Smith's arrival must have contributed to the billiards world in Shanghai. Smith can be said to have not made this trip in vain.

Masterful Skills

The eight performances in four days clearly show us that he is proficient in all kinds of other shooting methods. He is truly an all-rounder. What he considers to be his best skill is to pre-lead the opponent's ball to the left and right of the red ball's position, send the red ball with one shot, and the original ball rolls next to it, forming a triangle. Then open it up, send red, and circulate each other. It saves effort and makes it easier to score points. The Shanghai new record of 670 points was also achieved.

Gongying is Unique

The people selected to attend the performance on the Shanghai side were Li Gongying (three times), Liu Fuzong, Xu Shizhang, Kang Busi, Bo Tuo, and Medina (once each). In terms of the skills they showed, Li Gongying was the most popular. In front of the world famous players, he showed his ambition. His attitude was calm and his results were good. It was commendable. The other gentlemen were also able to work hard and specialize, and both advantages and disadvantages were visible. However, Medina did not play well last night. His usual performance can be on par with Gongying, but he completely lost his normal state last night.

People and Talent

— Chun Zhu

In one day, I discovered two things—two absolutely contradictory things.

In the morning, a friend named Peng came to see me. He's involved in education, so we talked about the situation in the education sector in Wu County. He said: Education in Wu County can't be considered backward, but the overcrowding of teachers is unexpected. There are already more than seven hundred people registered with the Education Bureau who don't have jobs. Among them, only about one-third are graduates from regular normal schools. The rest are from various schools, even university students and students who studied abroad. Because they can't find other opportunities, they're willing to settle for this cold bench life.

I couldn't help but click my tongue and say: This can truly be called an abundance of talent. It's a pity that so much talent has been buried. How pitiful!

In the afternoon, another friend involved in the chemical industry came to see me. He said: Our factory now wants to hire someone who has specialized research in the chemical industry. Knowing that you have wide connections, I ask you to help find someone.

I still had the morning's matter on my mind. I couldn't help but laugh and say: There are so many talented people in Suzhou. For a factory like yours (a medium-sized factory with 10,000 to 20,000 capital), can't you find a suitable person? Surely you're not looking for someone particularly extraordinary.

My friend laughed and said: To be honest, we've already advertised in the newspaper. Quite a few people applied, including many with specialized industrial degrees. We invited dozens of those we considered qualified to talk, but they were either completely clueless or just spouted empty words. There was absolutely no one who could actually do the work themselves. It's not that we look down on people, but we can't afford the masters and PhDs of foreign origin. The domestically produced talents we can afford are not suitable. Even if there are any, they've all become some kind of "technical officers" or "technicians" and wouldn't deign to come to a factory to work hard. Otherwise, why would I bother to ask you?

I laughed and said: If that's the case, I'll have to politely decline. Because I haven't seen anyone like you described.

After my friend left, I grumbled about unrelated things for a long time. It's said that it costs 100,000 yuan to educate a student abroad and 100 yuan to educate a primary school student. From the abolition of the imperial examination system and the establishment of schools in the late Qing Dynasty to now, over thirty years, I don't know how much money has been spent. What we've created are just many "(people)," not "(talent)." So, on the one hand, we cry "overstaffing," while on the other hand, we still feel a "lack of talent."

Who created these two contradictory phenomena? Probably the authorities in charge of education and the famous figures leading education for the past few decades must bear some responsibility? Especially those friends who treat students as experimental products, with a new "ism" every three days and a new method every five days.

Random Thoughts on Celebrating the New Year According to the Old Calendar

— Cao Wenhai

The Republic of China has been established for twenty-three years. Although government offices adopted the Gregorian calendar long ago and newspapers also switched to Gregorian dates, the common people still habitually use the old lunar calendar, and this entrenched custom is unbreakable. Two years ago, the National Government issued an order to the whole country to adopt the Gregorian calendar and abolish the lunar calendar. Party branches at all levels once extensively promoted this, and the government repeatedly admonished, no less than issuing three orders and five injunctions. However, observing all the recent actions of the common people, the image of celebrating the New Year remains. The New Year's rice cakes in the cake shops, the melon seeds and peanuts in the dried goods stores, the tea snacks and candies, and the meat and fruit shops, etc., their retail business is unusually busy. The wives and grandmothers in the mansions, the maids and elder sisters, and the shop clerks in the various stores, etc., are bustling about all day long, an endless stream, which shows a glimpse of respect for the New Year.

Recently, at night, various shops and wealthy families have even held "Year-end Thanks," offering whole pigs and whole sheep to the Kitchen God and other deities, making grand displays, staying up all night, with gongs and drums, and firecrackers, disturbing people's dreams. Every time at this time, setting off firecrackers for "Year-end Thanks" causes sparks to rise high, scattering on the roofs, inevitably causing fires. Those who suffer the disaster are mostly poor families. At a time of biting northerly winds, their homes are burned, leading to hunger and cold, which is also a matter of extreme joy turning into sorrow.

Walking into the City God Temple in the South City, I saw stalls lined up, like an open-air market. Recently, the best business is drawing monthly calendars, narcissus, orchids, wintersweet, and Nandina domestica branches from flower stalls, and children's toy stores and firecracker stores, etc., are also making three times the profit.

When it comes to the Gregorian New Year's Day, those who are elders often give silver dollars to the younger generation, called "lucky money." Ordinary ignorant children use this to buy sweets and learn to gamble, which is a waste of unconsciousness, which is a pity! During this Children's Year, parents should save their children's "lucky money" for them, accumulating little by little, wouldn't that be a blessing for the children?

The above-mentioned matters are deep-rooted bad habits that have been around for thousands of years. Ignorant and foolish people are not worthy of deep blame. But those who claim to be the intellectual class also follow the customs and do not make any effort to get rid of the old and bring forth the new, or make any plans to change customs and habits, which is what we do not understand.

A Visit to Tan's Tomb

— Cheng Zhizheng

Generally, anyone who has been to the capital will always want to visit the mausoleum of the Premier. Indeed, at the foot of the majestic Purple Mountain, the Premier's mausoleum is naturally the only building that can be called magnificent. However, in addition to Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum, I feel that there is also a Tan's Tomb that is more elegant and more serenely beautiful.

Tan's Tomb is the tomb of the late Premier of the Executive Yuan, Tan Yankai. It is about three li to the right of Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum, and just behind Linggu Temple. This year, I happened to be in Nanjing on business. After my friends took me to the usual Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum, Ming Mausoleum, and Five Continents Park, they talked about how elegant the newly completed Tan's Tomb was, so we decided to pay our respects.

After leaving Zhongshan Gate for about seven or eight li, the car stopped in front of Linggu Temple. Although Linggu Temple has now become a leisure resort for important people, after going inside, it is just a very ordinary temple. Tan's Tomb is right next to it, perhaps because Premier Tan often came here during his lifetime!

At the entrance of the tomb, there is a huge stone tablet, which says "Monument to the National Funeral of Premier Tan." It was inscribed by Chiang Kai-shek, the Chairman of the National Government at that time. Moving forward, the road is paved with gravel, and ancient trees with intertwined branches grow on both sides. Gradually climbing the mountain, a memorial hall is revealed in front of us. The memorial hall is purely in the palace style, with painted beams and carved pillars, beautiful and pleasing to the eye. In the center is a portrait of Premier Tan. Eulogies from various important people hang on the four walls. On the table are silver shields and silver screens, which are especially worth seeing, and there are several pairs of porcelain vases, about four or five feet high, arranged very exquisitely.

The memorial hall only has one room. After leaving the memorial hall, I searched for the tomb on all sides, but couldn't find it. I thought that maybe the tomb was just below the memorial hall, but I thought that it wouldn't be so simple. My friends led me up the mountain again, and after turning a few bends, Tan's Tomb was indeed reached. The tomb is made of cement, and in front of the tomb, white stone steps with railings are carved. On both sides, there are small pavilions, also in the palace style. From the entrance all the way to the front of the tomb, there are pots of fresh flowers.

The tomb is halfway up Purple Mountain, looking out at Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum and Ming Mausoleum, they are precisely in a mutually supporting position. The forests are vast and boundless, and the sound of the spring is gurgling, what a serene place for eternal rest!

After sitting for a while, I followed the original path down the mountain, and next to the memorial hall, I discovered a memorial park. This park was donated by the Hunan Provincial Government, because Premier Tan was from Hunan, and the Hunan authorities at that time were the old subordinates who were most deeply favored by Premier Tan. Therefore, this memorial park was also built very exquisitely. In addition to flowers and trees, there are pavilions and halls, springs, and small bridges, as well as memorial inscriptions praising his merits, which shows how deeply Premier Tan was missed after his death.

After visiting Tan's Tomb, I felt that Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum was indeed magnificent, but it was unobstructed and lacked twists and turns. Although Tan's Tomb is small, the land is secluded and the terrain is obstructed, with plenty of changes. From entering the National Funeral Monument to reaching the tomb, it is a full half a li, sometimes hidden and sometimes visible, winding several times. The designing engineer must have put in a lot of effort.

Finally, I hope that tourists who visit the capital in the future will never forget this good place - Premier Tan's Tomb.

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Fourth

Drinking and Passing Food, Madly Celebrating, Containing Farewell Tears

Picking Up the Lamp to Warm Dreams, Singing Softly Through the Long Night

Zi Qiang answered casually: That's right, in about half a month, it might snow outside the pass. When Zhao Weng heard these words, he couldn't help but feel his heart skip a beat, and he immediately thought, what if a war breaks out, what should I do? So he closed his eyes and pretended to be thinking intently about something. At the same time, the two tears that were about to roll out were also closed in his eyes and did not come out. Zi Qiang didn't dare to sit here anymore, and saying that he was going to tidy things up, he also went back to his room and lay down. When it was time for dinner, Gui Zhi led Zi Qiang to the hall, and he saw four large plates placed in the center of the table, filled with things like sausages and oil-soaked chicken. Two large plates of meat pies were placed diagonally across the table, and a brightly lit white-shade kerosene lamp was shining below, along with a tin wine pot. Gui Zhi sat down at the bottom, pointed to the empty chair on her left hand, and said: You sit down. When Zhao Zi Qiang saw his father and mother-in-law sitting on the other two sides, he laughed and said: Placing the table in the middle, with four people sitting on four sides, it looks like a feast. Gui Zhi picked up the wine pot and poured wine into the empty glass on the left, and laughed: As the saying goes, the gift may be light, but the sentiment is heavy, sending a goose feather from a thousand miles away. This is just a feast of two large plates of meat pies, but my good intentions are true, and you should eat it as if it were a feast of shark fin and bird's nest. If you agree with what I said, then first drink a toast. Zhao Zi Qiang didn't say anything more, picked up his glass and drank it dry in one gulp, and even held it up to take a look. Jiang Shi, holding her chopsticks, laughed and said: Our young lady, you're even more eloquent today. Gui Zhi laughed and said: Is this considered eloquent? I'm still planning to talk to him all night long. As she spoke, the wine pot in her hand had already stretched out in front of Zi Qiang. Zi Qiang held his glass with both hands and accepted her wine, and laughed: I have to return the toast, right? Gui Zhi hugged the wine pot to her chest, and laughed: No, today I'm seeing you off, I'll save it until I go to Qian'an, and you can drink it to welcome me. (313)

Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

The Evolution of Vacuum Tubes

— Yi Zhi

Foreword

Wireless radio has only been around for a little over thirty years since its invention, but the rapid progress it has made should be attributed to the vacuum tube, the soul of wireless radio. Since the English Fleming created the diode, it wasn't long before tetrodes, pentodes, heptodes, AC tubes, and filamentless tubes appeared one after another, numbering over a hundred. With so many vacuum tubes, their characteristics are becoming more and more complex. If I were to describe the evolution of vacuum tubes in detail, this publication's limited space would not allow it. Therefore, I will only select the more important ones and briefly describe them in categories below.

Diodes | Triodes

In 1884, Edison added an electrode to his invented vacuum bulb and discovered a current phenomenon. Scholars at the time could not explain the reason and called it the "Edison Effect." In 1886, the Englishman Fleming applied Edison's phenomenon to create a diode for detection and rectification. In 1889, Thomson and Richardson explained the working principle of vacuum tubes with the electron theory, saying that when the filament is heated, it evaporates electrons, which are then attracted by the positively charged plate, forming the Edison effect. In 1907, the American De Forest added a metal mesh grid between the filament and the plate in the diode, greatly increasing the efficiency, and created the triode. In 1915, the American Longmirm increased the vacuum of De Forest's soft triode, making it a hard triode. At this time, the triode had reached its development peak and could be used for oscillation, amplitude modulation, detection, and amplification.

Tetrodes | Pentodes

Triodes used for radio frequency amplification are prone to oscillation and add noise due to their large interelectrode capacitance and electron reflection. Therefore, the German Schottky and the American A.W. Hull invented the tetrode, such as UX-22. Its structure is to add another grid, called the "screen grid," between the grid and the plate of the triode. This tube is truly unexpected. Its high radio frequency amplification, small interelectrode capacitance, good sensitivity, and good selectivity are far superior to triodes. However, due to the limitations of its characteristics, this tube can only be used for radio frequency amplification. Researchers added another grid between the screen grid and the plate of this tetrode, connected to the cathode, to prevent the secondary emission of electrons. As a result, the plate current increased greatly and the output power was very large. It is most suitable for amplification in the audio frequency range, and is called the power pentode, such as the 247 tube.

AC Tubes | Directly Heated, Indirectly Heated, Rapidly Heated As wireless telephone became increasingly developed, it was uneconomical and troublesome to supply the vacuum tubes of radios with dry batteries or storage batteries. Therefore, AC tubes were created. Initially, there was only the directly heated type, which reduced the filament resistance of the triode to reduce AC hum, such as UX-226, etc. Later, an improved type was created, called the indirectly heated type, which isolated the filament from the cathode. The filament is only used for heating, and the cathode is only used for emission, such as Uy-227, etc. The AC hum of this tube is very low, but the filament must pass heat to the cathode through an insulator, so the vacuum tube of this type operates very slowly. Therefore, it was further improved, with the insulator piercing through the air, so that the cathode could obtain the radiant heat emitted by the filament, and the operation could be faster, called the rapidly heated type, such as the new 227-224-A, etc.

Dual-Grid Triodes | Twin Triodes, Dual-Plate Triodes, Dual-Plate Pentodes | Heptodes

Ordinary triodes, if the input signal voltage is too high, will cause distortion, so the dual-grid triode was invented, such as the 46 tube. The input signal can be increased by one time compared to ordinary triodes. Also, according to the principle of push-pull Class B amplification, two triodes are placed in one tube, called the twin triode, such as the 2B6 tube. To avoid the increasing complexity of the circuit, one tube is used for multiple purposes, such as detection, amplification, and volume control, or radio frequency amplification, intermediate frequency amplification, oscillation, etc. Therefore, dual-plate triodes (Diode Triode) such as 55·85 tubes, etc., were made. There are also dual-plate pentodes (Diode pentode) such as 2B7·6B, etc. There are also heptodes such as 2A7·6A7, etc.

Special Vacuum Tubes

American 又創一種無燈絲式管（Ｆｉｌａｍｅｎｔｌｅｓｓｔｕｂθ）更因無綫電影與超短波之研究突飛猛進·有陰極綫電視管Ｃａｔｈｏｄｅ　Ｒａｙｔθｌｖｉｓｊｏｎ　ｔｕｂｅ及鞋紐管　Ｓｈｏｅ　ｂｕｔｔｏｎｕｂｅ等發明·

美国又创一种无灯丝式管（Ｆｉｌａｍｅｎｔｌｅｓｓｔｕｂθ）更因无线电影与超短波之研究突飞猛进·有阴极线电视管Ｃａｔｈｏｄｅ　Ｒａｙｔθｌｖｉｓｊｏｎ　ｔｕｂｅ及鞋纽管　Ｓｈｏｅ　ｂｕｔｔｏｎｕｂｅ等发明·

Cathode and IIOV high voltage tube High tension tube manufacturing,

The United States also created a filamentless tube. Furthermore, due to the rapid progress in the research of wireless film and ultra-short waves, cathode ray television tubes and shoe button tubes were invented.

Conclusion

Vacuum tubes have reached their peak, but European and American researchers are still working hard. Although we cannot predict how they will develop in the future, judging from the current situation, the internal structure of vacuum tubes will become more and more complex, and one tube will be used for multiple cycles, which will be more effective than the latest 2A7 and 2B7 tubes.

Vacuum Tubes for Detection

— Gao Chongling

The components in a radio receiver that perform the function of detection can be divided into two categories: one is the crystal in a crystal radio, and the other is the vacuum tube.

Vacuum tubes for detection (Tube as detector) are an indispensable component in vacuum tube radios, just like the crystal in a crystal radio. Every radio must have at least one detection vacuum tube. Superheterodyne radios are even divided into first and second detection vacuum tubes. For example, the vacuum tube in the simplest one-tube radio is the detection tube, the two-tube radio has a detection tube and a low-frequency amplification tube, and the three-tube radio has a high-frequency amplification tube, a detection tube, and a low-frequency amplification tube, etc. (To be continued)

Mr. Zhuang Zhihong, the manager of the company, is not only good at repairing radios, but also has a deep understanding of repairing sound film machines. It is said that yesterday, the machine of a major cinema suddenly stopped working. It was repaired by famous Western technicians in Shanghai many times, but it could not be restored to its original state. Later, it was repaired by Mr. Zhuang, and it was completed within two hours, and the sound was even better than before. The company's exquisite technology can be seen from this. Chinese people who have radios and need repairs may want to give it a try.

Currently, the factory employs more than 2,600 workers, and there is still a shortage of manpower. Therefore, more workers will be hired in the near future.

Rural farmers who have not purchased a radio can borrow to listen at places where radios are available, in order to ensure that all German citizens can listen to the broadcast on this day.

Pound against the dollar rose to .625, while the dollar against the pound rose by 2.75%. The pound against the franc fell by 8.2 centimes, while the dollar against the franc rose by 1.025 centimes. London spot gold rose by 3 pence. Private cables showed the silver price rising by .1875, with exchange rates up by 2.5%. In morning trading, the near-term settlement price opened at 1 shilling 4.25 pence for the pound and 33.875 yuan for the dollar. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Bank's listing revealed the dollar up by .125, the franc down by 6 francs, and the mark down by .75, with the rest unchanged. In the afternoon, banks engaged in exchange rate arbitrage, and the process remained flat, with the situation fluctuating. Securities: "Consolidated Six" Public Bonds See Strongest Gains

Bullish Traders Tend to Abandon Troop Reduction and Consolidate "Consolidated Six"

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange was open for the last day of the old lunar year. Despite being the tail end, trading was not desolate. There was quite a bit of floating short covering, floating longs, and spread trading in the morning, settling accounts. Due to the holiday break, which spans nine days, preparations had to be made to avoid risks. However, most traders were still waiting to see what would happen after the "red board" reopening. With only four days remaining until February delivery after the reopening, market prices would not suddenly drop if the environment remained unchanged. Still, the supply and demand of chips should be the benchmark for price fluctuations. In the morning opening, short covering and buying-in were evident, and market prices rose uniformly by 0.12 to 0.45 yuan, with this month's "Consolidated Six" seeing the strongest gains. In the second session, some long traders covered, resulting in a slight decline, approximately 0.12 yuan. In the afternoon opening, the "50 series" and others were still in demand, and the upward trend did not diminish, recovering another 0.1 to 0.4 yuan. The closing was slightly chaotic but generally saw more gains than losses, mostly by 0.12 yuan, while "Consolidated Six" recovered another 0.45 yuan. Throughout the day, the trend of the most extreme "troop reduction" increase was only 0.05 to 0.1 yuan, due to heavier selling of "16 series." "Consolidated Six" saw the strongest gains, due to active buying of "17 series" and "33 series," coupled with short covering. As a result, this month saw a gain of 1.15 yuan, while the far term only saw a gain of 0.5 yuan. Bullish traders tend to abandon "troop reduction" and consolidate "Consolidated Six." As a result, market prices mostly saw gains of around 0.23 yuan, with near-term "Consolidated Six" alone gaining over 1 yuan, leading all bonds. The total trading volume was 13,443,000 yuan, including 3,000 yuan in spot, 4,885,000 yuan in total salt tax futures, 1,980,000 yuan in "troop reduction," 1,095,000 yuan in "19 Customs Revenue," 1,435,000 yuan in "20 Series 20 Customs Revenue," 2,665,000 yuan in gold short-term "Consolidated Six," and the rest in the range of 200,000-300,000 yuan.

Silk and Tea: Spring Sales of Silk Initiated

(Lyon White Filature Again Reports Rise) Yesterday morning, the local French silk trading house, Sinvoux, received a telegram from the Lyon silk market stating that B-grade white filature 13/15 denier had opened at 69 francs per kilogram, up 2.5 francs from the beginning of the week. This translates to an increase of over 10 yuan per bale in Chinese currency. Although there was no change in A-grade on the surface, calculated by the franc exchange rate, each bale also secretly increased by 5-6 yuan.

(Douppioni Silk Printing Sales Remain Brisk) The demand for Indian douppioni silk remains brisk. Local inventory in Shanghai is thin. In the recent decade, British mail ships have loaded 80 yuan worth of douppioni silk, shipped to India via England.

(Shanghai Silk Market Also Shows Firm Rise) Silk merchants in New York, Lyon, London, and other ports have already implemented restrictions on the sale and use of Japanese silk. Furthermore, with the initiation of spring sales, the consumption of raw silk has increased sharply, inventory is gradually thinning, and factories are diligently importing. The Chinese silk market continues to show an upward trend. Various European and American firms in Shanghai have started buying. The market atmosphere is increasingly firm. Yesterday, firms from England, France, and other countries imported 70 bales of yellow and white filature, with prices rising sharply by 20 yuan.

Tea Houses' Green Tea Exports Still Strong

The tea market for foreign firms in this port has seen very few transactions recently. This is because the tea suitable for sales in the market is extremely rare among Chinese merchants, and the lower-grade goods from lower-end firms have stagnant sales channels, resulting in a market with no activity. However, the various green teas that foreign firms imported last year, such as Luzhuang Zhenmei and Zhenmei needles, after a large portion had been weighed and delivered, still had over 20,000 boxes. In recent days, firms such as Xiehe, Jardine Matheson, Jinlong, and Xiezhuhui have been transporting and paying for these teas separately. Today, the French Postal Shipping Company's Asia Express is exporting 8,000 boxes of Luzhuang green tea delivered by various foreign firms. It is said that a large batch will continue to be shipped out during the next shipping schedule.

A Review of the Woolen Fabric Market in the Past Year

Still Inferior to the Year Before in Terms of Overall Observation

Autumn and Winter Seasonality Outperforms Spring and Summer

Last year, the woolen fabric market was still inferior to the year before, indicating the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the decline of urban industry and commerce. The market conditions over the past year, including price fluctuations, are summarized below:

(January) Apart from cavalry twill and checked worsted showing a firmer trend, the rest were sluggish and declining. This was due to the approach of the end of the lunar year, and buyers were cautious about importing goods. (February) Spring sales began, and goods of all kinds were selling briskly, especially in high demand from all directions in the street. However, the opening prices for the "red board" were generally cheaper than in 1932. This was because the pound sterling had lengthened, which lowered costs. Fortunately, the arrival of new goods at the port was very scarce, allowing prices to be maintained without falling. The reason for the lack of new goods arriving at the port was that factories abroad had previously gone on strike, resulting in delayed deliveries. (March) Various goods with delayed deliveries from foreign factories were shipped to Shanghai one after another, causing prices to plummet. Yuanzhigong plain serge and worsted, etc., became even more chaotic. Fitted materials such as Hanling bouclé and flannel showed a firmer trend. (April) Prices became even more fatigued, with both apparent and hidden weaknesses. The woolen fabrics of the same brand sold for vastly different prices, and customers often negotiated to drive prices down. This was supposed to be a peak sales season, but the market atmosphere was sluggish, due to oversupply, combined with inconsistent costs of new and old goods, the impact of Japanese dumping, and unstable times, which weakened the purchasing power of customers, creating such a situation. (May) Flannel, hemp canvas, summer white goods, and the like sold very smoothly. However, the market price continued to decline without showing any signs of recovery. After the new tariff rules were announced, many goods changed from ad valorem tariffs to specific tariffs, increasing the cost of woolen fabrics, and prices gradually began to rise. (June) Due to the increased tariffs, various wool textiles that were in season gradually rose in price. The industry association once petitioned for relief but was denied, which further strengthened the market trend. However, plain serge and thin floral worsted fabrics around 4 yuan were still in the lower reaches, because of a large batch of Japanese goods being dumped in Shanghai. (July) It was the height of summer, and there should have been a pause, but merchants from Sichuan suddenly made large purchases. Domestic camel wool, Yuanchang yellow-grey worsted, thick plain fabric shoe felt fabric, East China serge floral fabric, etc., saw many transactions, which boosted the market atmosphere. (August) The woolen fabric market made great progress, and prices also turned firm. There were transactions from customers in Tianjin, Sichuan, Peiping, Qingdao, and the Yangtze River region. Western-style suit fabrics were even more popular, and merchants in the industry were optimistic about orders. (September) Except for plain serge, which was heavily impacted by Japanese goods, other goods were better than in August. Purchases from local and outside customers were strong, and prices were firm both domestically and externally. The British firm, Dodwell & Co., first announced an increase in the price of standard woolen fabrics, and as a result, many firms followed suit by raising prices (this month can be said to be the best of the entire year). (October) The trend was similar to September. In the second half of the month, woolen fabric postal packages suddenly decreased, and customers from all regions temporarily stopped adding to their purchases, because starting from the 18th of this month, the post office suddenly wanted to collect taxes on woolen fabric packages. (November) After the woolen fabric industry association worked to negotiate with the authorities, the authorities immediately understood and canceled the postal package tax, allowing deliveries to be accompanied by customs import permits. As a result, the number of woolen fabric export packages remained congested, and the market atmosphere was good. Although there was news of Fujian's independence, it did not have much impact. French washable floral fabric, cavalry twill, and three types of cavalry twill were especially strong and active. (December) Foreign firms raised prices, and the selling prices of thick and thin goods remained firm. However, sales were slightly sluggish, creating an atmosphere of apparent firmness and hidden loosening. Coupled with pressure from East China goods and the end of the Chinese calendar year, shops were carefully extending credit and seeking to recover debts, and transactions gradually decreased.

Free Talk

Year-End

— Fan Zhongyun

After the New Calendar Year comes the Old Calendar Year. For us poor people, the New Year is indeed a significant hurdle, truly living up to its name as the "Year-End Hurdle."

With the Year-End Hurdle arriving, debts come all at once, and with empty hands, it is extremely difficult to get through: this is the first difficulty. Moreover, with the New Year approaching, a joyous festival, there must be timely decorations and social interactions among family and friends. However, with empty pockets, what to do? What to do! At this time, in the deep of the night, listening to the sounds of firecrackers everywhere, it feels as if each sound is hitting the heart. Counting the days until the end of the year, it is only a matter of a few days, but such time feels like a year passing by.

Most unbearable is that in the past, there was only the Old Calendar Year, but now, with the addition of the New Calendar Year, we must pass through two Year-End Hurdles each year. At the end of the New Calendar Year, shop transactions and bank overdrafts must be settled. However, new activities must wait until after the Old Calendar Year. Thus, between these New and Old Year-End Hurdles, we are like fish trapped in a dried-up rut, forced to struggle and die. Today, we seem like Wu Zixu passing through the Zhaoguan pass, passing one hurdle after another. With our hearts burning with anxiety, we unknowingly find that our temples have suddenly turned gray.

Being in the intersection of the old and new eras, this is our inevitable fate. Because such phenomena are not limited to the New Year alone, but are true in all other aspects.

Many people, for the sake of neatness and convenience, have changed to Western clothing. However, upon returning home, they feel the comfort of Chinese clothing. Thus, wardrobes must contain both Chinese and Western clothing, and cloth shoes and leather shoes must be purchased simultaneously.

Furthermore, in the family, traditional women, although capable of managing the household, are not skilled in social interactions. Modern women, on the other hand, are highly skilled in social gatherings and interactions, but not good at managing the household. Thus, husbands, for the sake of the family, do not know what to do.

The old is worth cherishing, and the new must also be adapted to, thus we suffer to the extreme!

Habit and the times force us to pass through two Year-End Hurdles, and thus we have become victims for no good reason.

How to Eliminate "Shanghai Style"?

— Yi Jun

Since someone from the North began to mock the so-called "Shanghai Style" writers (referring to some degenerate elements in the Shanghai New Literature scene), the non-"Shanghai Style" writers in Shanghai have also felt the need to speak out. A few days ago, someone in "Free Talk" clearly stated that "the non-'Shanghai Style' writers in Shanghai should rise up to clarify themselves, and there is no need to trouble the 'Beijing Style' writers to launch a distant expedition." This shows that the hatred of evil is a universal feeling. Kicking those shameless literary scoundrels out of our New Literary world is indeed the right thing to do!

However, so far, the attacks have been limited to the realm of pure literature, which I believe is incorrect. In my opinion, the movement to eradicate "Shanghai Style" should be extended to the entire writing world.

Those current affairs commentators who have others write articles for them, relying on flattery to beg for the pity of the chief editor and get them published, and then go around deceiving and swindling; those authors who hire a large number of literary slaves at home, copying and pasting from magazines and newspapers to plagiarize and turn them into books, and publish them under their own names; those international experts who don't understand any foreign languages, but rely on clerical skills to hire a few extremely bored translators to translate Japanese into Chinese and then Chinese into English, and publish them under their own names, taking advantage of all sides. Aren't these precisely the practices of "Shanghai Style" writers? Why hasn't anyone come out to attack them? Is it because everyone's mouths have been stuffed shut by a meal and drinks from these "Shanghai Style" writers?

In my view, these "Shanghai Style" writers are more evil than those Shanghai Style novelists. Although they are unlearned and incompetent, their methods of scheming and maneuvering are first-class. They often have the magic power to control cultural institutions and can exert extremely bad influence on China's cultural and writing circles. I believe that to eliminate "Shanghai Style" writers, we should start with these types of people.

What are the methods to eliminate them? It's hard to say what the active methods are, but passive methods are easy to implement:

(1) Self-respecting publishers (including newspapers, magazines, and bookstores) should refuse to publish their work;

(2) Self-respecting writers should refuse to cooperate with them (such as if they run a publication and invite you to be a special contributor, or if they run a school and invite you to be an honorary professor, etc.);

(3) Self-respecting young people should not be kept by them, not be used by them, not write, compile, or translate for them, and not be accomplices. In this way, these "Shanghai Style" writers can slowly disappear. They will understand that the cultural world is not something that can be bought and sold empty-handed. They will embark on the path they should take || becoming officials or doing business || and will not continue to cause trouble in the cultural and writing circles, causing the entire Shanghai New Cultural scene to be tainted with an impure name.

New Year's Eve

— Bai Yan

In the blink of an eye, New Year's Eve is approaching again.

In a foreign land, I always feel a surge of emotions during festivals; the distant dreams of my childhood cannot help but float to the surface of my mind.

In my childhood, how I loved New Year's Eve! At that time, I could wear new clothes, I could play with firecrackers, and I could feast on delicious food. Moreover, even if I made minor mistakes, my mother would not punish me harshly...

However, during my tenth year, that New Year's Eve left me with an impression that was quite difficult to forget.

That day, Uncle Yong (my father's friend) came to our house very early. My father had him sit down in the study. Not long after, my father went out on business. Only he was left alone in the room. Sometimes, my mother would occasionally enter the room to talk to him for a few sentences, but he would answer in such a shy and quiet voice. I snuggled beside my mother, curiously watching him, because he was not usually like this. Why was he distressed when people felt joy during the New Year? After leaving the room, I whispered to my mother.

(Mom! Why is Uncle Yong hiding alone in the room?)

(He's playing 'Emperor' (Note 1)!) My mother said softly.

However, I still couldn't understand my mother's answer. I just secretly peered at him through the crack in the window.

In the room, he just wandered around aimlessly, and sometimes he would sit down quietly, looking very distressed with his brows furrowed. He would sigh softly from time to time.

All day long, he just locked himself inside the walls.

It wasn't until it was time to light the lamps that he quietly slipped out the door.

At that time, I didn't understand anything about the flavor of life. I just observed everything with surprised eyes. As I grew older, I realized that New Year's Eve was just a New Year's Eve for the rich; for the poor, it was another "hurdle"!

(Note 1) "Emperor" is a refined term used in Huizhou for someone evading debts.

Final Reply Regarding Realistic Novels and First-Person Perspective

— Mu Mutian

Because of the issue of "realistic novels and the first-person perspective," I had some tangential debates with Mr. Chen Ye. Mr. Chen, grasping at shadows and indulging in high-flown rhetoric, strayed further and further from the point. It's best to conclude this.

My motive for raising that question was that, after reading "Literary Arts," I saw several works by young people inappropriately and lazily using the first-person perspective. To correct this, I wrote that article "On Realistic Novels and the First-Person Perspective."

My conclusion is that realistic novels must have their unique style. Literary styles are time-bound. Realistic novels must have their fundamental style, which occupies the dominant position. However, old styles can continue their remaining life to a certain extent. New content can be put into old styles, but the old style cannot become the dominant style. Therefore, realistic novels should mainly use the third-person perspective. But that does not prohibit the occasional use of the first-person perspective. However, using the first-person perspective to express large subjects, broad and complex realities, is prone to problems no matter how well it is controlled. For example, in "Germinal" (by Émile Zola), it would be difficult to write so thoroughly, no matter which character is used for self-narration. If Mr. Chen wants me to give examples of new realism, then "The Rout" (by Alexander Fadeyev) is a good example. Also, works like "Water Margin" naturally cannot be handled using the first-person perspective. However, in short works with simple subjects, in appropriate situations, the first-person perspective can still be used. But this is limited to a very narrow scope, like "Hunger" (by Knut Hamsun) and so on. But that cannot become the basic style of realism. It is not permissible to regard it as equivalent to the third-person perspective.

In China today, using workers and peasants as protagonists makes the first-person perspective even more difficult to use appropriately. If workers and peasants were to write themselves, it would probably not become a work of art, because Chinese workers and peasants are mostly illiterate. If intellectuals were to write their confessions, the emotions and tone would be very difficult to make authentic. Therefore, in China today, the first-person perspective will again be limited to an extremely narrow scope. But this does not mean that works depicting the lives of workers and peasants cannot be produced in China today.

The above is my conclusion. Let me further analyze Mr. Chen's mistakes. Mr. Chen's spirit of debate is admirable. However, those points of negligence should be overcome.

(1) Mr. Chen has consistently engaged in abstract and empty talk. He has not engaged in practical discussions based on works. He thinks "Yang Ma's Diary" is acceptable. In fact, everyone knows it goes against reality that an old nanny can write such elegant diaries. He says: "Use the first-person perspective when it is appropriate," but he did not indicate which work has used it appropriately.

(2) Mr. Chen distortingly and one-sidedly uses his materials. He categorically affirms that Gorky is a "great realist" while obscuring Gorky's romantic side. He quotes Flaubert's criticism of Zola: "He writes the language of hooligans when writing about hooligans," and misattributes it by saying: "This is the classic that authors must read when producing realistic novels in the first-person perspective." He forgot that "objectivity" and "detachment" were the creeds of 19th-century realism. Which of the "Rougon-Macquart" novels is written in the first-person perspective? This is what I want to ask.

(3) Mr. Chen specializes in distorting other people's arguments and subjectively and arbitrarily developing them. I said: "In China today, where culture is backward, writing novels about workers and peasants in the first-person perspective is more likely to become farcical." But Mr. Chen has distorted it to mean that novels about workers and peasants cannot be produced in China today. Such deliberate distortion, followed by a deceitful rebuttal, is truly "Pigsy filing a complaint against the plaintiff." I think this kind of "debate policy" is not good.

(4) Although old realism and new realism have differences, they also have their similarities. Mr. Chen has again understood this point one-sidedly. Although the two are based on different worldviews, they are the same in demanding "truthfulness." The characters portrayed must be living, real people, which is their common requirement.

(5) Mr. Chen mechanically separates content and form. He even more mechanically believes that not using the first-person perspective means being in the position of an outsider. We have always affirmed the consistency of content and form. One cannot explore form without connecting it to content. Mr. Chen has not yet understood this point! It is not that using the first-person perspective in a novel can make the author inseparable from the masses they are writing about. "The Rout" is a practical example. Isn't "Yang Ma's Diary" the same?

Finally, Mr. Chen has misunderstood the truthfulness of literature. Perhaps my wording was flawed on this point. Naturally, I am opposed to writing realism as simply listing and piling up. Realism wants to express all aspects of reality and their relationships, which is undoubtedly the case.

Let this issue end here. Originally, I thought that in principle, I didn't have much difference with Mr. Chen. There was originally a long reply, but the editor of "Free Talk" asked me to shorten it due to space constraints. Therefore, it has only now been abridged into this piece.

Editor's Note: Discussions on this issue will end here. Future submissions from either party will generally not be published.

I Curse Your Smile (3)

— Wu Yan

One day, he came to our store to buy something, saying the name (Jie Wu) in Burmese. He assumed that people living in Burma would understand Burmese. Immediately seeing that everyone was confused, he made a circle with his thumb and index finger, and said again:

(Jie Wu, Jie Wu...)

The two diplomatic talents in our store, the proprietress and her eldest daughter, painstakingly tried to guess what (Jie Wu) meant.

(Mango?)

The proprietress thought that every time he came to the store, he would always buy some of the newly picked fruit, so she said that. Then she pointed to the mango tree outside the door, to see which fruit the Indian wanted.

The Indian shook his head, his face flushed, and he became anxious.

(Jie Wu, Jie Wu...)

He said repeatedly, spitting out each syllable, making a circle with his hand. However, the Foreign Minister proprietress also failed. Who could guess it?

(I know, I know.)

The daughter, who assisted her mother, suddenly exclaimed, and ran into the kitchen, her wooden clogs clapping loudly. She happily carried out a bamboo basket of potatoes, and ran out clapping again, holding it high in front of the Indian, almost touching his brown nose. She excitedly said:

(Is it, is it, is it... you dumb person!)

But the Indian was still shaking his chin, but his face was even redder, smiling unnaturally, wanting to say something, but unable to, very anxious.

Thinking she had guessed correctly, but the result was still wrong, she was exceptionally disappointed. The bamboo basket softly drooped down, she pursed her lips, and cursed fiercely at the Indian:

(You're going to die! Indian devil!)

Naturally he didn't understand, but he understood that he was being cursed, and showed a very sad expression.

(Don't listen to his nonsense!)

The proprietress saw that the business that had already come to the door could not be done, sighed, and sat on the side, opening the black cloth of her chest, pulling out her nipple, stuffing it in her child's mouth, gently rocking.

This Indian, trapped in a desperate situation, turned into a mute, suddenly became clever, slightly bent down, squatted on the ground, stretched out his arms, flapping them like a bird, making this sound with his mouth.
