Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Chronicle of Events

— Yi Ping

After all, we are Chinese. After the Gregorian New Year, there is also the Lunar New Year (or the Abolished Calendar New Year). Friends who write articles naturally write timely articles whenever they can. After the Gregorian New Year, they write a "New Year's Trial Pen." For the Lunar New Year, they come up with "New Year's Greetings, Success in Everything." But my heart is pounding, and I stop breathing for a few seconds when I hear the doorbell ring. It was like that during the Gregorian New Year, and it's still like that now that the Lunar New Year is coming. But I have to write, just like I have to eat, precisely because writing articles = (equals) eating. So I picked up my pen and wrote the three words "Chronicle of Events." Then I thought that doing this kind of "archaeological" work is thankless. Collecting evidence of the Minbian rebellion, or the bustling return of a certain important person, if I'm not reading the newspaper while sitting on the toilet, there's definitely no need for me to nag again. But my personal big events, like borrowing money, being scolded, etc., seem like "family scandals should not be aired." Looking at the weeping red candle, I really can't think of any big events worth recording. But when I wrote the title, it seemed like there were many big events to record, so I lit a cigarette. Even if I'm squeezing oil from a stone, I have to write some things that I consider to be "big." After all, I'm a smart person. I remembered that the bosses of the cigarette companies, understanding that writers don't have stimulants to squeeze their blood when writing, manufactured so many cigarettes, the magnificent Navy Cut, the perfect My Dear, Wang Dao, White Dragon, Old Gun, British Brand. To thank them for their kindness, I think the first item to be included in the Chronicle of Events is...

On a certain day of a certain month, the Huacheng Tobacco Company placed full-page ads in Shen and Xin newspapers, Beautiful brand reduced sales by 40 cents per tin, and 10 cents per pack.

The lottery tickets of Shen Dacheng had universal gifts such as meat noodles and fish noodles, and the one customer of the Sanyou Industrial Society (that is our in-laws) can be regarded as the pioneer of this year's advertising.

Audel Pierre arrived in China and was "enchanted by Chinese women (for several days)." (Here I can give a thumbs up and say that my wife is a "Chinese woman.")

Domestic films inexplicably (changed) (an exception to the exception), foreign films greatly (reversed). (an exception to the exception)

A certain pharmacy on Mintini Yin Road hangs a sign saying "(Ruyi X Great Sale, selling for 20 cents each)."

Haikingbo arrived in India fully loaded.

This summer, the number of women with exposed ankles increased by one-half compared to last year, and rouge changed to turmeric.

Mei Lanfang and Li Guichun unprecedentedly collaborated on a new play, "Five Iron Duke Ties," also known as the Beijing-Shanghai Struggle.

The Great World had two visits from strange people. The Great Thousand World had one visit from a magic master.

Falsely claiming to be kidnapped is this year's new method for avoiding debt.

The Nine Stars Theater performs hula dances and other physical performances once a week.

Two new hotels opened, three large cinemas, countless Chinese medicine shops, and countless banks.

New film queen Chen Yumei, Emperor Wildcat married.

There are more than 100,000 radios in Shanghai. The sales of lullaby records reached more than 20,000.

The comedian Wu Neng passed away.

Two major assassination cases occurred.

A sex-related suicide case was discovered.

Rue Joffre was renamed Mysterious Street.

In this year, the rural economy collapsed. Chronicle of Events finished, farewell to the pen!

With the sound of firecrackers, we bid farewell to the old,

Peach charms bring renewal to all things.

Note: The above are all calculated according to the abolished calendar.

"(High Hats)" and "(Entryway Smiles)"

— Tong Zi

In today's society, if you want to make a living, and you go to relatives and friends for help, you always have to prepare some gifts to show respect. These respectful things are called "(Entryway Smiles)."

Judging from the name of these three words "(Entryway Smiles)", we can know the importance of this thing: with an entryway, you can buy people's smiles, which is a good sign (?). So, if we want to find something to do, we have to ask relatives and friends, we must be cautious, and spare no sacrifice or cost to buy people's smiles. You must know that without an entryway, people will not smile, and if they don't smile, it's not good?

But, people always come out to find food to eat because they are poor, and they go to beg relatives and friends in order to find food to eat; the reason for bowing their heads and asking people for help is nothing more than wanting to get something done, a little bit of money. Before things have been accomplished, they have to spend a sum of money, isn't this worrying?

Moreover, "(Entryway Smiles)" are not something that can be done carelessly. If used properly, it is auspicious, if used improperly, it is ominous. The things you give to people must be to their liking, at least they must be generous and appropriate; otherwise, if you offend people and embarrass them, then not only will you not be able to buy a smile, but you may also provoke them to be unkind?

Therefore, "(Entryway Smiles)" are simply a stepping stone to seeking things, and also a head-on blow to seeking things.

I think: people always like "(compliments)", and respectful gifts are nothing more than "(compliments)"; if the "(compliment)" is good, you can get a smile. But, the "(compliment)" of a gift, first, must be affordable, and second, it must be agreeable to the recipient; if it is unaffordable, you cannot "(compliment)" people, and if it is not agreeable to the recipient, it cannot be a "(compliment)". Given these many difficulties, it is better to use "(high hats)", which are simpler and more economical.

The original title of "(High Hats)" is "(flattery)", also known as "(bootlicking)". Our belly is the main camp of this thing. We can use our tongue as a visiting card for gift-giving. This kind of "(entryway smile)" that does not cost money is inexhaustible. If we want to ask someone for help, it doesn't matter if we can't afford a gift, as long as we give him a "(high hat)".

Everyone likes to wear "(high hats)", there is absolutely no reason why they wouldn't like them! As long as we send one, two, three, four, five, or six hats, are we still afraid that people won't smile?
